Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are attached to the roots of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, and appear as ugly and rough growths; sometimes the teeth themselves become black, green, or yellow, as corruption spreads to the gums, and they emit a foul odor; you should have the patient lean forward so that his head is between your hands and his teeth are visible to you, then pick at the growths or discoloration until nothing remains; likewise with black, green, or yellow stains, clean them off completely; if they come off at first attempt, all the better; if not, repeat the process the next day or the day after, until everything is removed; know that teeth require different types of instruments for cleaning, depending on what the condition presents, so that the scrapers used to clean between the teeth have different forms from those used to clean the teeth themselves; these various forms and others should be prepared and ready.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When treating a toothache, you should not rush, but take as much time as possible, for there is no excuse for causing pain during the procedure.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is forced to pull, you must be certain of the tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he thinks it is in a sound tooth, and makes him pull out a good tooth; and yet the pain does not go away because of this, as long as the evil tooth remains, for we have already tried this with those healers. And when you are quite certain of the decayed tooth, you must scrape around the tooth to the gum all around, then press it hard with your fingers or with fine tweezers at the front and back, until it is well loosened; then grip it firmly with the tweezers, and let the patient's head be between your knees, and hold it steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Afterwards, pull out the tooth carefully without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and put it inside on each side gently, then move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, then you should fill the holes with pieces of cloth, and gently hold it with tweezers so that it does not break while being held; and one must work carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be sure to take care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it behind, causing greater pain due to the malicious root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware of doing as ignorant surgeons do, who in their haste and arrogance sometimes break the jaw, not heeding what we have instructed; they sometimes bring about great illness due to the roots that remain, or by breaking the jaw, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, wash the area with wine or garlic and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the site; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shape of the instruments with which you pluck out teeth first should have long points and broad handles so that they do not break when you pull on the tooth. The shapes are:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of strong material so that they do not bend when pulling, and made of good iron, and have teeth to hold the gums.
de la racine des dens	from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in place, you must place wet cotton soaked in butter on it for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the area is soft, then insert the tweezers that are called 'algefri', which make the shoulder look like a sick bird's beak; and inside they should be shaped like a file, that is their form.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with all these tweezers, then you should uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is to say a spatula, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and wide so that it does not break, and if the root pops out through this, that is good; if not, then use all the instruments, of which the shapes come below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one should use this instrument with two edges, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in the reason of teeth, and of this instrument which looks like large tweezers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong enough that it cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise master finds his own instrument according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are many diseases in which the ancients did not teach an instrument because of their diversity; and if it does not break in the cart or other bones, or it protrudes, then he seeks the instruments that he needs, as I have told you, and aids with gestures, by which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and strong enough to hold the bone, so that it does not slip, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines, and if there is a protrusion in the bone, and it is small, then cut it with all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to nature's form, and its shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you should know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down; then pull it out; and if there is an abscess with the tooth, then take this instrument of which the form is like a small beak, and let it be made of tempered iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And pluck it gently several times a day because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others; and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it with one part of this file as shown in the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the lime with which needles are made; and in lime the tooth little by little in the hand, so that it does not move until it breaks; then smooth it at the end with a file, and if the tooth is too sharp and it pierces the tongue, it should be filed down so that it is even and does not pierce the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth has a hole in it from either an impact or by biting, and the patient cannot press on what he is eating without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines but it does not work; then they should be restrained with a gold wire, because silver wires become green and rotten, but gold never moves. The wire should be medium-sized nor too thick or thin, according to the amount of space between the teeth. If you want to move the teeth, take the wire and wrap it twice around the two healthy teeth, then put the shoulder in between the teeth, whether there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then restart the bleeding as far as where you began, and stretch your hand gently and bleedingly, so that it does not move at all. The bleeding should reach the tooth's root so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grip the head of the thread with pliers and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and put it in so that it does not bite the tongue; then leave it tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes loose or the threads break, tighten it with another thread; let it remain and serve like this throughout its lifetime, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy and two diseased teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and experienced should attempt this, for sometimes they make the shape of a tooth from cow's bone, and put it in the place where there is a defect, and bind it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	cut the vein of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament which comes under the tongue is congenital; sometimes it is caused by a wound. The treatment is to open the mouth of the patient, press his head against your healthy teeth, and lift up his tongue; then grasp the broad ligament with tweezers as far down as the tongue can be separated from its bed, and if there is any swelling or nodule - which indicates an abscess - cut it out. Be careful not to make the incision too deep so as not to injure the artery underneath. When you are done, rinse the mouth with rose water or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue; every night smear the wound with pitch so that no scabs can form.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is bleeding, place powdered vitriol on the area; and if the blood stops, cauterize with a lentigo cautery, which is good for this. Then treat it further until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see the vein is dark or black and hard, and the patient does not feel any pain, do not touch it because it is a ulcer. If it is declining to become a blister and there is moisture, cut it with a spatulum, freeing it from both sides. If bleeding occurs due to your action, apply ground vitriol until it stops; then return to your treatment, pulling everything out; then raise the area with garlic and salt, and treat the wound further until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there are sores in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called almonds, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they do not heal, be careful: if they are hard abscesses of a small size and dark color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for fear of bleeding; but let it be until it is cured, and then you will burst it, or it will burst by itself; and if it is a white color with a thin root, have the instrument to cover it, but first look to see if the abscess is calm and pacified.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and have his head in your lap, and open his mouth and hold his tongue between your fingers, and press down on the tongue under all the instrument, from which this is the shape; and it should be made of silver or thin bronze just like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Then you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, grab it with the tweezers and pull it up into the almond, and draw any threads of the warts with it; then cover the instrument, which is shaped like a needle, so that it appears sharp; and yet the ends are curved, one towards the other, and they are very pointed, and it is made of iron or bronze:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then cover it with tongs, shaped like a needle:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	Let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other, and when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other according to this same method; then after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water, and with water and garlic, and if there is bleeding, gargle with water, or with the peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or with myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses other than the two tonsils appear in the throat, so cut them then as you did the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and she had a very tight closure all throughout the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway which was blocked, and she could not eat or drink, and would have died if she stayed like that for another day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had become so swollen that it had forced out two bumps through the two openings of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hurried therefore, and stuck in the hook into one of the openings, then drew out a large piece of pus; then I did the same on the other side of the nose, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards, I stuck the hook into the abscess, and scooped out a portion, and only a little blood came out; thus the passageway in her throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and wine, and continued to cut into the abscess for a long time; and the abscess re-grew and filled up the space that I had emptied, so that it became very large; therefore, I lanced it and cauterized it inside her throat; thus it did not grow any more; and I left these parts, and do not know what happened to her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the eye descends to the socket and it is swollen and long, it is called 'perpendicular'. And if it is fat and round below, it is called an 'eye'.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the pus in the abscess is settled, and it is subtle, then you should cut it; and one that is round and not long; and if it is blood-red or dark red or black, then you should avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it according to the manner that I have said, from its white and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it out, and cut it at the one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you should not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it will hurt the voice and speech. And after the incision, use what we said about the incision of the two testicles, and treat it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears being cut, then you should use the cautery of the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of the cautery is for acute pain.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in yours, and then presses his tongue against the instrument we described in the chapter on cautery, and breathes in through it with live coals, so that it is not too thick or too thin; and use the shaft of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And on the head there is a hair or place where medicine is applied, like the edge of a spoon, and the instrument is placed on all the medicine over the iris; and the patient should lie on his side, so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth due to the medicine inside, so that it does not go down the throat and into the lungs. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it against the iris for about half an hour, until you see it become numb and the stinging of the medicine subside; then take some cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the eye so that the cotton is pressed against the iris; do this frequently until the cautery is complete, then leave it to dry and fall off after four or five days. If you need to renew the cautery with medicine, do so, and afterwards rinse the eye with cold water, and treat it with gargarisms until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calamin, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, avens, and similar herbs, and mix all or some of them in one pot, and add garlic, and let it boil. The pot should be well-glazed with strong clay, and the instrument inside should be bent according to this shape:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it can be made of silver or bronze, and one of the ends should be pushed into the mouth of the patient so that the vapors rise into the uvula through the tube until the uvula is deadened. Then he should do this often until the uvula dries out, and take care not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, because many things can happen there; nor should this be done beyond the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put an egg white inside the tip, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; because the egg white will not let the vapor weigh down the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times there is a bone or fish spine, or some object stuck in the throat; therefore, you should try to remove whatever you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all your strength, so that you can move the object; and if it does not come out and is stuck in the throat, you should make the patient vomit until the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting. Or the patient might swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a dry piece of bread; tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it; when it reaches the spot, it will get stuck, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out in the way we have described, take an instrument made of soft lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the tip so that it can enter the throat more easily, and the tip should be lifted upwards; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, or it may cause harm, and do not push the os down; and move the patient's head so that they can swallow the instrument, in order for them to dislodge the object; then, they can either swallow the instrument, or you can pull it out along with the object.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the bleeding is medicine, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient facing the sun, then press his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the bleeding, draw it out with a small hook, or with fine tweezers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a heated iron wand and put it in the patient's throat, then put the hot end of the wand on the shoulder, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take clean water in a glass, open the mouth and pour it in without swallowing, and move the jaw frequently with their hand; as soon as the patient feels the water, they will spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not spit out as we have said, then suffocate the patient with assafetida, using the instrument that I described for fumigation of the throat; do this many times, for it will come out without harm.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way to do the fumigation is to take a pot with burning coals, and have the container covered with a perforated lid, and in the hole place the head of the instrument; then pour in the smoke, and have the patient put their mouth over the end of the pipe, closing their mouth so that the smoke cannot escape, but goes into the throat; and the blood will come out now, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient be thirsty, eating salted and dry things, and drink no water; and then it will be necessary for them to go to the toilet.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats hemorrhoids, when one can see it, resembles bent tongs in order to be able to enter the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and it has roughness like sandpaper, so that what it seizes, it cannot let go; and here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the abscess-draining instruments
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to what recollections come later in this book from one person and another, and they vary in penetration and size; and there are two kinds, one is in its appearance the same, and that which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is due to the locations in the body where they occur.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundations, and the abscesses of fleshy places are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own treatment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And for some abscesses one must not pierce until the bowels are dead according to their fulfillment; and there are others which one must pierce when they are crusty, and they do not die according to their fulfillment, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses occur near joints, and one lets them be until they are soft all around, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may become corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.Et si on les percet tant qu’il sont crut, li membre est en perile de contractere, car ne poent le nerf et li lien se remuer ains qu’il soit curat; et si on les laisse porris entor, si sont li membres en gran danger.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay piercing it until it has reached its peak, it will harm the principal member; or if it is near the foundation, pierce it so that it may be cured; but you must not pierce an abscess without digestion being complete, except for one that is near the foundation, lest it burst inside and lengthen, causing a fistula which will take a long time to heal.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is necessary for you to know the time of piercing the abscess which is dead according to its fullness, and that is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and from the discharge and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary for you to make the piercing at the highest point of the abscess, and where there is movement; and let the piercing be long in the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and on nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	For those who bend, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to let it be until digestion is complete and confirmed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before then, the body will be filled with poison from the abscess, and the lips and depths of it may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if on any abscess that are pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat small abscesses with small openings; and large abscesses with large openings, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are abscesses where one should cut into the core, and cover it; when it has become as soft as a drape, and is deadened, then one should do as one does with blisters: and there are some that are split in three angles; and there are some which one covers just like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the bowels; and there are some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions, and similar covering.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, like a superficial abscess, one should pierce it plainly; and when the abscess is large, and has drawn great pus, and you pierce it, then one should not draw out all the pus in that hour, but some part of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more; do this several times a day, until all the pus comes out; likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying child, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the expert sometimes jumps with the release of wind, which by chance kills the patient, and you do not notice.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution; and when you have perceived your abscess, open the wound and examine if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a flat wound, apply tents made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess with many openings, you should insert a tent in each opening so that they face each other; and if you have cut into the skin around the abscess and pulled it forward, you should fill it with old cotton or the shavings of linen fabric without moisture, and bandage it for three days; then remove the bandage and treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs due to your work, bring cold water and a cloth, and hold it over the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding continues, apply treatment and healing, and the powders I have described earlier in this book. If it is during winter, and the area is very nervous, you should place warm tents and moistened cloths in wine and hot oil over the wound for a third of a day, as we have said; then open the abscess, wash and treat it, as it should be, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And now you must understand universally about the treatment of abscesses; I have told you how one should go about treating abscesses, and you will find this chapter [on the subject].
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the neck come small abscesses, which are similar to those that appear on our heads, like the spots on a guinea fowl, and there are many kinds of these.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some which have fat and such where there is moisture as well as pulp; and there are some which are hard and stony in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause opposition.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the shoulder is that you should test with every instrument which is called a 'dislocation', whose form comes later, depending on what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they will draw it out from above the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, they scorch without leaving anything behind that contains the moisture, for it will return as soon as something is left there; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain overnight will be cured.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then return to the cotton, as before, on the second and third days, until you are sure that it is not sore at night; then clean the wound with ointment, as appropriate, until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains pus, then open it according to this method: cut it lengthwise, and squeeze out the pus from all sides, and apply all your treatment to drawing it out above the wound; and if the artery beats strongly, do as I have told you before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also treat an abscess if it is stone-like, and cut and clean it as I have told you.Car la piere adessourve li tuit la membre por quoy elle gist, et al cote ou elle est adessourve, et le membre adessourve li tuit de la cotte ou il gist; et la cotte a l’adessourvance de la piere.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the stone hurts all around where it lies, and the part where it is located hurts, and the limb hurts all around where it lies; and the skin hurts at the location of the stone. And cutting into the stone-like abscess and the moist one is easier, because they are filled with pus and blood.Car si li aposteme est de sang ne puce, il est de poque de sang et de sanc, et al pletz du corps ou il gist, car li sang al pletz s’en va.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there is no moisture in any of these abscesses on the head, and there were some that I copied from the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if anyone had cut it, it would have made a wound just like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come on the head, except those that occur on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should be made in the most dependent part to allow the pus to flow out; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere in the body; they are large and interconnected with each other.Ande leu de ces apostemes, si est qu’il vait la pluit et la fumee, li ou il ne vait pas, il faut que l’ovre et qu’il cure le mues, et que il li ovre et qu’il cure la piere aussi; car il est maintes foiz la piere dedenz l’aposteme, et s’il n’est pas ovree, et ne est la piere extraite, il ne peut gueres guarir.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its coat, as the nodule and abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many resembling these scrofulae.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are wicked ones that will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Therefore, in that one which you see to be of good disposition for cauterization, and resembling the color of the body, and flat on each side, and not raised towards the nerves of the neck or the artery or the channel, and not deep; you should cover it from above, and scrape away at each part, and have the two lips of the heart at an angle, if you need to, as we said about abscesses in the head; and draw it out little by little, and be sure that you do not cut into the nerve or vein, and let there not be an ague nor trembling so that the hand does not shake, and do not look too far ahead, so that you do not cover anything that you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	If you grasp the vein or artery and it does not yield to your touch, then put into the wound vitriol ground up, or some powders that stop bleeding, and tie off the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed down and the wound softens and begins to suppurate.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work until you have completed it; then examine with your finger if there are any small scrofulae remaining, and pick them out and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, you should not pick out that scrofula at its root, but ligature it with a double strong thread and let it hang loose without harm; then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut away the entire scrofula, then you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now so that there remains no superfluity due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you should proceed to cut away its root, and draw it out, and sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas which hold superfluity, pierce where it appears to be dying; and pierce it thus as the one before was said, depending on it, then minister tenting with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is remained of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, then cure it with ointment enjoining flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	[of scrofula]
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients wrote and spoke of throat surgery; but I have never seen anyone in our land perform it, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squinance, it is necessary to cut into the throat, which is called the "epiglottis"; and one should not hesitate to do this, because all the veins and the lung of the patient are affected by the heat of the abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the lung, one must cover the epiglottis to prevent asphyxiation due to strangulation.Si li maladie est en la gorge et qu’il soit necessaire de le fendre, il covient que li fendure soit a l’epiglote, ou li maladie ne pueda aver finne; car la est lor mort.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we should split it underneath three circles or four a small split crosswise between the two circles, or according to the quantity of the split in the hyoid bone; and those places which are subject to the section of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then he should stretch the skin of the throat to its fullest extent, then split the throat as far as the voice box; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then close the wound, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe of the larynx which jumps out through the opening that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which one doubts the strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and cut all the way to the cartilage; then administer remedies that promote the growth of flesh, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuchasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely choked, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the lack of air has ceased.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe in, and he will breathe out through the wound, and thus is preserved from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease passed, which passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, once it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a maiden take a knife and thrust it into her throat, cutting part of the windpipe; and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I exposed the wound and found that blood had come out of it, and judged that it had not bled well or been treated properly before, as the blood was still flowing from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound and healed her until she was cured; and the maiden had no more trouble with her voice, and returned to her usual state; hence I say that one should have no fear of cutting into the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This type of abscess is called a "hernia in the throat", and it is a large abscess the color of a plum, and it occurs frequently in women; and there are two types: natural and accidental; the natural kind has no cause.Accidental hernia occurs when something blocks the throat so that food cannot pass through, or if someone drinks too much wine and gets sick, causing food to ferment in the stomach; or if someone drinks cold water after eating too much, and causes the stomach to swell; or if someone drinks too much wine on an empty stomach, making him sick.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident happens in two ways, one of which is similar to a boil on our bodies, and the other way is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and one should not operate by making force except in the small one, and test and search throughout the entire wound: if you find it as hard as a nail, and it cannot be opened in any way, then cut it, just as nails are cut, and treat it all over its surface, if there is none; and search thoroughly, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many types of boils, and I will describe all their appearances; and now I must explain the entire difference between a boil and an abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is when there is a fever and heat, until the ebullition has passed and the porridge is complete; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a boil, there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body; and it begins just like a pimple, and becomes large; and they have two appearances, either dry or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.And li nouts ne doivent mie eslonger sur la chair, si com les issues, car il conviennent que li nout soit adont qu’il esteit, et li issue se move et va par tout le cors; et sont selonc ij maniere, ou sec, ou moiste: selonc la maniere qui est moiste, est selonc ij semblanz, ou selonc aposteme de artere, ou selonc nout de gras.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you come to the treatment of the cold, first test and examine it with all the instruments that are called "intramural", according to what its form will lead to in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses in the brain is to press on the wettest place that you find in the abscess, and gradually turn your fingers, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core; then, depending on the size of the abscess, draw out the instrument, and be careful not to push too far.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the pus flows freely, whatever its color, treat it as I have described for other abscesses; and if after the instrument is withdrawn no pus comes out, know that it is solid, so treat it in a cross shape, and grasp it with pincers, and carefully scrape each side and remove the dead tissue where it lies, so that you draw it out healthy with the nerve; and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then cut it away in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing is done, the nose will return many times; and if something is done to stop it for a little while, and the wound is not painful, apply some corrosive powders and bind up the wound with hot poultices, and treat it with other remedies until it heals; and if the nostril is large, cut off the two edges of the wound, and treat it with remedies that cause scabs.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the bleeding vessels are contrary or elsewhere, and you are in a hurry, use powdered vitriol, and leave it for two or three days until the wound suppurates and the blood stops flowing; then return to treating what has been delayed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the trocar, which are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three types of handle called 'albaret', and one type called 'breb'; and there are also three kinds: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the aperture of the fistula; and they are like needles used to pierce sorcerers' marks, made from brass, iron, or silver, but the yellow ones are best and most proven, made from black lead, for treating fistula.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	There are many forms of warts, as you can see: large, medium, and small; some have two curves in three ways; some have three curves and are also in three ways; some have two curves and warts with only one curve, and they are in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The tips of these knives are sharp, and some only cut one side, so they don't damage the vein or nerve; and with these instruments, warts are removed from many places, so that the patient does not suffer when opening an abscess; and there are three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they are only used on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas; and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling slices of fingernails, according to this shape, with which blood is stopped.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the place that heals by cutting off the veins, and the arteries, and sometimes they are tied according to this great shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	The nipples of some men become swollen when they become corrupt, appearing like women’s nipples; they remain ugly and swollen, and if one wishes to cure them, one must apply the cautery according to this method from line b to g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scorch the fat, and treat the wound with ointment containing charcoal, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and heal it until it is cured; and if the nipple hangs down and becomes soft due to its size as happens to women, then cut it into two slits at the top, so that one slit is attached to the other at the end, so that the larger slit holds the smaller according to this form, from line b to g; then scorch the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, until it is cured; and if it is not cured, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood flow, then you must fill the wound with wet cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it absorbs the remainder of the fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the testicles
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses which come underneath the armpits are types of hard scrofula where there are nodules and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this shape, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus within the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with clean cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, they should be treated as we have described for fissures of scrofula, and if the wound becomes swollen, they should apply a cautery as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	from bleeding of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is open and the skin above it is attached, this often leads to abscesses; and so too when it affects the vein and becomes swollen and abscessed. One can tell which it is by the nature of the abscess: if it is due to the artery, the abscess will be long and deep; but when it is from the vein, there will be a red discoloration visible. It is foolishness to cover this type of abscess, especially when located under the nails or on the fingers and toes, as well as on the neck and in many other places, since it can become very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore one should avoid cauterization with iron, and when it is on the head one should also avoid cautery there; if it is an abscess due to the artery opening under the skin, one must make an incision along the edge of the artery until it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath, piercing through to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places according to how I instructed you regarding the extraction of the two temporal arteries. Then tie off the area between the two threads with a ligature, so that the blood flows out from the vein; then treat it with an appropriate poultice until it heals. If the abscess is due to an incision in the vein, one must take some of the pus and smear it over all the skin around the abscess, and then insert a needle under where one is holding the pus, piercing through to the other side, and tie off a double thread so that you can draw out the pus; then bind the abscess as I described, at either end with the thread; if you are worried the thread will slip out, insert another needle under the entire abscess, following the incision of the first needle, and tie off the threads in four places.
