Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is fresh, suspend it and cut it; and have blood-stopping medicines such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, and egg white; then apply a wide piece of cotton so that the wound does not close; and let it be for a long time, and apply a linen bandage; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there is fresh flesh in the wound, it must be cut in this way, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Because one should not touch an abscess that is in a wound.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood flows habitually, and when hemorrhoids are old they become gangrenous; and we have already described their appearances in the section on diseases of the anus, and I will now describe those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the testicles, when they are completely inside the anus, and do not appear on examination, are not cured by an iron cautery.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the mouth of the anus, which one can feel, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore you must put the woman in a cold room, then pull out the hemorrhoids with tweezers and cut off their roots, then powder them with medicines that constrict blood vessels, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there is a flow of blood, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, then take barley flour and mix it with honey and garlic, and make a poultice from this and apply it to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it is stopped up, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, then make him breathe through a tube in the back and on the breasts without bleeding; then take a cloth, soak it in plantain juice or dogwood juice with old wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has burst, then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red and looks like rough leather, so cover it as I have said before; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come in the genitals, such as sores and perianal abscesses and herpes and cysts and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases which I have described in the classification.Quant li sang est en l’herberie et ne peut adont être tire par veine, si covient il que tu li fai une incision sus la piere; car par celi le sang sortira, et apaisera li mal.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess which comes in the stomach, which is not one of those which collect in the bowels; and if you wish to know the treatment for iron, then look to see whether the abscesses are soft at the beginning of their appearance, and full of heat and fever, and whether they turn red when you can see them.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not rush to pierce it, but let it be measured as long as the pain is relieved; and then let the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats on which he can lean, and support his back, and bring his feet together at the sides of his legs; and let his thighs be spread out, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good rope; then suck the navel towards the right side, and administer the instrument to open the mouth of the stomach, from which the form then comes; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument being administered, that you insert the rod first to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters with the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the wound with cloth so that the instrument does not hurt him; and he must place the funnel of the instrument at the top, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and they are made soft in the hand, then it is necessary to cover with the head of the spatumile; and when the bowels are emptied, you should put into the wound moist tents in rose oil, or in dry green oil; and put the tent beyond the wound at the bottom of the injury, and put by pressure on the injury and on the little finger a clean linen moistened in water or mallows cooked; then cure after two days of ointment occurring to this, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the injury and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and aristologus cooked for a long time; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is wrapped in the injury, it is necessary that you beware of cooking with iron, but cure as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary for the midwife to first understand the natural process of childbirth and its signs: when you see the woman push downward and desire to smell a rose, then hasten the child's emergence; thus you will know that this childbirth is following the natural course, with the baby emerging head first, and the placenta following; and when you see these signs, gently press her belly so that the child is born promptly. For when the baby emerges head-first, the placenta follows, and the mother's excesses are cleansed through proper purification; and this is how it should be for a natural birth. But if it happens otherwise, it is not natural.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Sometimes the baby emerges feet-first, or head-first but turned to the side, or by the arms or hips; it may also emerge from the stomach or armpits. If the baby is born in an abnormal position, the midwife must be wise and skilled in these matters, cautious of error and deception, and I will show you how to assist in all such cases.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes headfirst through a natural birth, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her vitality is weak, then make her sit on a stool or have other women hold her up; and anoint her private parts with oil or fried fenugreek, and then the midwife should insert a little spatulum (as described below) into her:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the afterbirth, and press on its nail until the moisture that is within flows out; and squeeze the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then the woman should be enema with a mixture of fenugreek and sesame oil; then make her sneeze and cough up phlegm, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then the child will come out now.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out, then you should gently reset them a little bit at a time; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a chair, and lift her feet up; then stand the chair on the ground, and hold her so that she does not strain while standing; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then grip the hands with the knife as mentioned above, and extract the child, and reset in the same way.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the birth of a child from its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out from its feet, it should be pushed upwards; then it is turned little by little until it is even; then grab it by the feet and stretch it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to its hips, instruct it to be grabbed, and cause it to sneeze with incense; if it leaps out, so be it by God's will.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, then gradually return it to its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have described, take musk, tall oil, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar; then apply this ointment to the woman's womb, and make her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is softened below, place the myrrh collar on her and let it stay for an hour; then make her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and pinch her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child will come out soon.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	the infant will emerge onto his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this way, place your hands on his head gently; then lie him on his side, with his feet hanging down, and let him lie on his back; and fold his hands gently, and then press his hands on his belly, and lift up the cushions underneath, until he is positioned downwards; and if the child does not cry out, take his feet and move him gently, then move his belly upstream, then place your hands over his mouth; and rock the child gently; and command the woman to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the exit of the child who comes out of a width of one hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must try to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then let her sit on the bed, and raise her legs gently; then administer the mucilage which I have described; and if she does not give birth, then let her sit on a chair, and try to bring back the hand; and rock the child according to nature, and make her sneeze, and command her to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the baby emerging from his mother's neck, and spreading out his hands, and turning his face towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary for the bailiff to dye his hand, then turn it slightly and slowly, and move it gently; and when it is equalized, he places on the nature of mushroom and oil, as we have said, then he commands that it moves little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command her to grip; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way with all the membranes
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way to all the afterbirth, then grab the afterbirth with your fingernail, as long as the moisture is drained; and if the child can on his face and neck, he grabs her by the throat, so that she is not held back, and the child dies; then bottle the child inside, as long as you have placed him as it should be, and command the woman to grip several times: then he will recover gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the discharge of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You know that twins are often born, and sometimes .iii. or .iv.; and it is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	They are strange things and do not live if they are not named; I know that they are multiplied and separated by the syringe that divides them, which is attached to the udder; and sometimes they emerge as naturally as a tail, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge quickly, then the midwife should act as we have said, and be quick and skillful in what she does; and act as is best for the mother's health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed inside the womb with 1, or 2, or 3, or 4, or 5, or 6, or 7, or more up to 15, and they are all shaped like children according to the measurement of the glorious sage; and the midwife should know all this because sometimes strange things happen; so act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman for a stillborn child or abdominal pain, as I said in the previous section, and there is no quick delivery, and you are forced to use manual intervention; then you should know if the woman is of sound health and has no fear of death. Then the woman should be laid on her back, with her head inclined downward and her legs raised. The midwife should apply the teats from both sides, or strap her to the bed so she does not move while delivering the child. Then grease the mouth of the mother with moist oils infused with myrrh, fenugreek, and flax seed; then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and myrrh; then gently insert them into the mother, and find the place where the child is positioned so it can descend onto its head. Then insert the teats into her own orifices: in her throat, her mouth, her palate, under her beard, near her ears, or on the sides of her neck if the descent is toward the feet; insert them into the armpit and the lower ribs if the descent is sideways. The midwife should hold the teat in her right hand and place a cord between her fingers on her left hand, and gently stroke the teat from hand to tip, then insert it into one of the orifices we have mentioned until she reaches the empty space. This is how the teats should be used:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then pierce against the other knuckle, or the third if you need to, so that the extractions are even; and then they are even as they move from one side to another, to move out, and the knuckles are bitten to hold them in place, as is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some remains, then anoint the ball of one of his fingers with oil, and press it into that part, and pull the other part; and if nothing remains, then put this knuckle or a higher place, and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be pulled back because of the tension, then you must wrap a cloth around it until it comes out; then press on the joint of the palm or the wrist, and so you should do with the other hand, and with the feet as well.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	If the child's head is large and constricted in the birth canal, and there is a great accumulation of fluid, you must insert the spatumile between your fingers, puncture the head, and release the fluid; or use the instrument called "almidach," with which the shape comes out along with the instruments or chapter that follows this one. In the same way, if the child naturally has a large head, then pull on the bones with forceps, and if the head pops out and is stretched by force, split it so that the fluids in the birth canal are released; and if it cannot be released, cut it into pieces as much as you can. And if the child is swollen in the abdomen or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the fluids flow out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on his feet, and the pulse is light, and the pulse in the throat is weak.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If the child is constricted in the abdomen or pelvis, you should stretch it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and puncture the abdomen or pelvis so that the fluids inside flow out. If other limbs are stuck and the head remains, insert the balling instrument into the mouth of the birth canal, grab hold of the limb, and pull it out. Then, insert one or two fingers and pull the rest out. If the mouth of the birth canal is narrowed by a hot abscess that has formed there, you should not attempt to force anything in; instead, apply moist and greasy substances, and use poultices soaked in warm, softening fluids.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on his back, and you can put him straight, then do as we have said for a living child; but if they are unable, then carry him by parts, leaving nothing of the placenta behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if pus comes out as we have said for abscesses that come in the womb; and if there is bleeding, then it should be stopped with a tourniquet, and other treatments should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose fetus had died within her belly; then another was sewn on top of it, and the other one died too.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she developed an abscess in her armpit, which swelled up and opened, causing a foul discharge.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat her, and I thought about it for a long time, but couldn't find a way to heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed strong attracting plasters on her, and some bones came out, and after a few days, some more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed because there are no bones in one's belly.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted to wound and put my hands in there until the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived for a long time like that, and then she suddenly died a little bit from that place; and I have not heard of this chapter being used except that when a master finds something strange, he should know how to apply a remedy.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the dislocation back into place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	After that comes the form of the pulley, which is found in books; and with two turns at each of the two shoulders.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the probe should be more flexible than the restringent, and it should be made of boxwood or ebony; and the mouth of the probe should be two digits wide, and the rim of the trees should be one-and-a-half inches long; and in both sides there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are tightened on one side and loosened on the other, half an inch long or a little more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the womb to open it when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with its appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of tweezers; and has two adjustments at each end, as you see, a palm-length long, and two fingers wide; and when you see to open the wound to the whole instrument, then let the woman lie on the bed, her feet hanging down and her legs spread apart, then fit the two adjustments together in the wound, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs; then work your hand to the whole instrument, as you have done with tweezers equally, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the wound, until the patient makes the face she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all surmounted, and their appearances are multiplied; and when the mirors have been prepared, the work is more swift, and men are higher for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair over the instrument until you have prepared it, for their necessity is inexcusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the placenta is retained at childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with some scent, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; and if she sneezes through it, that is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, he takes a pot and makes a cover for it, and puts herbs in it that can open the mouth of the wound, such as camomile, anise, rue, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over fire; then he puts one end of the pot into the mouth of the wound, and the other end on the wound itself, and lets the vapors enter the wound; then he makes her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the pus does not come out easily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she still has it after this treatment and it does not go away, command the midwife to moisten her left hand in oil of wormwood or in a poultice of alder, and then put it into the natural opening and seek the second membrane; and when she has found it, she should seize it and stretch it gently little by little, so that the wound is not damaged during extraction; but it must be moved slightly from side to side, and then pulled out; thus it will come out and be dislodged.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the wound is tight, we have spoken of the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it is not one of all those that we have said, then beware of fooling around the anus; but you must tie what is at the mouth of the wound to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse it with a four-drug ointment; then she will defecate and urinate, and it will come out; but still, when she defecates, there comes a bad smell to the stomach and head, and the disease blights.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Then one should use suitable fumigations: some of the ancients have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to smoke out the woman for the retention of flowers and afterbirth, if it is like this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is similar in appearance to a dog's head, and the narrow end is placed downward in nature, and the wide end is placed upward over the fire; and there should be fumigation over the coals, and the boil until it is wasted away, and then another one starts.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the uterus
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born with an imperforate anus; the rectum is closed by a thin membrane. Therefore, the midwife should pierce that membrane with her finger, and not with a sharp instrument, and she must be careful not to touch it with her nails; then she should apply warm milk mixed with wine and oil, and treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will close up again, put a piece of wood in the opening and leave it for a few days, then remove it when the child wants to go into the chamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this swelling comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess; then one must cover it suddenly: and it should be treated as we have said about the cane of splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that originate below the anus are caused by nodules, and grow larger as they approach the anus, or in between its two halves, there may be one or more fistulas; and when this nodule is old, it opens, and usually emits a white moist discharge or a thin fluid, and sometimes these fistulas are suppurating; they are caused by what comes out through the anus or rectum, or by flatulence when the patient expels gas, and occasionally a worm may come out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they have ulcers that pierce up to the bladder and halfway down the shaft of the penis; and they reach as far as the hip joint and the base of the scrotum.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula piercing in the anus, and not at all piercing: and it is that you push your index finger into the anus, and push a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twistiness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twistiness, push in a slender tent of lead or horsehair until you feel the tent with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no pus or wind or ver comes out as we have said, know that it does not pierce; then be quick about cleaning it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has pierced as far as the bladder or the passage of urine, and urine escapes, and it cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces as far as the joint of the thigh, then the tent comes out as far as the spot; if there is no twistiness and the pain is throughout the surrounding area, then it will immediately go away, and ointments are of no use; in these piercing fistulas there is no cure other than labor, and vanity of foolish remedies that interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one who is neither very young nor old, there is hope of recovery by cauterization with fire, as I have experienced, and the patient lies on his back between your hands; you lift his legs up to his thighs, and have his thighs bent towards his belly; then you insert a tent made of bronze, or of lead if there is any tortuosity, as far as you know where the tent goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain around his anus, then you must insert your index finger, unless of course the tent has already pierced him; and it should be uncovered where between your finger and the patient you feel either the sigmoid colon or the rectum, thus indicating that it is perforate; one should not operate on such a patient.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	Nevertheless, one can sometimes heal some people, but this seldom happens; and the treatment that helps is to heat the cautery subtilely according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; then insert it hot into the fistula all the way out through the anus, and do this two or three times until you know that the charred flesh, which looks like an owl's feather, has come away; then treat with moist tents soaked in butter, until those chars come out; then treat with ointment, binding flesh to flesh.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it does not heal thus; and the fistula enters and does not pierce to the depth which is in the foundation, and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of flesh or syphac, and you see the fistula continuing below the covering of the skin; then cut it open at the beginning of the fistula, and squeeze gently towards the tent, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the top of the tent; and the tent will be delivered, and will fall out; then remove those scarred tissues that look like a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the vein bleeds, and the blood flows between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or with a medication.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery draws together two things: that is, it burns those scarred tissues, and draws out blood and dries up moisture; then treat tents moistened with butter or crushed substances, until the place bleeds, and the burned flesh comes away in the bleeding; then treat the wound with ointments of hardening agents over dry flesh, and these are the remedies that are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes from the depths of the fundament, and is separated from the body, put in two fingers or the fundaments, and investigate it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and within it is the membrane or sac, or it is ready to burst, then do not go too deep that you damage the underlying structure, and let the discharge happen naturally; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or remove the covering and clean it once it has been cut away from the underlying structure, either by tent or another pointed instrument; then cleanse the wounded tissue as best you can; then work on healing the wound and keeping the fistula in the area outside the underlying structure. Thus the patient will be relieved of the discomfort.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas according to this manner: and when you pierce the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the underlying structure near the skin, then take a tent pierced at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a twisted thread into both, and insert the tent all along the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing in the margin of the fundament inside, then pull out the thread of that hole, as you would push your finger into the fundament; and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two heads together, and tighten them against each other, and leave it for one or two days; and sometimes restrain it, until the threads cut through the flesh that is between two; then cure the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, then have it burst in every way you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one must not bandage a wound that is so deep, but rather heal it, as we have said, until it is clean.Et s’ele est em parfont, si covient le lacement coper, et puis le cure, s’ele est em parfont, tant qu’il soit sanez.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spathumile spiny, from which one makes the fistula, is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other; and one should not cut into that which one should not cut into, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids occur in two ways: either they are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there can be small or large ones, and they ooze blood, and there can be one or more, and they protrude outside the fundament and at the top of the fundament; but those which protrude have less moisture, and still ooze a little bit of aqueous humor or a little blood, and they are the color of the body. The treatment for those who have them inside the fundament is that you instruct the patient to straining to defecate until the fundament opens and the threads become visible; then hurry and grab it with your fingernail or tweezers, and cut it at its roots; if the tweezers cannot hold them because of moisture, take them with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or from a piece of camel's hair; pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and dust them with hot powder that is used as cauterization; or cauterize them as it is described in the chapter on cauterization, then cure them with other cures until they are healed, and fear incision with iron. If the fundament cannot protrude, then cleanse the patient with a strong and harsh enema to wash away whatever is inside the fundament so that it can protrude freely; when the patient strains, and if the threads have come out of the fundament, then the cure is easy. You grab them with your fingernail or tweezers, cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed and fear incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must use stitching, do it in this way: take a twisted thread and put it through a needle, then pull the thread through from the top and push the needle through from the other side; bring both ends of the thread under the needle, and let them hang loosely; then tighten the thread, tie a knot, and remove the needle; do this for all the others, and leave one to drain away any excess blood; then put a damp cloth, moistened with rose oil or cerate, over the wound, and instruct the patient to rest; then let him stay like that until he feels better, and once he is healed, treat the wound with ointment and other remedies.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	drying from the heat or moisture of the bowels
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Drying of the bowels often occurs in the intestines due to natural constriction and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must cut away at the edge of a wound with a sharp object or your fingernail so that it does not become moist, then treat it until it is dry and healed as it should be; if it cannot heal, then repeat the cutting more aggressively than before, until it heals fully and is scarred; then treat it until it is completely healed.
dou fremit	where it trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ant is a small appearance formed under the body, and goes very deep; and sometimes the frost bites it, and they feel it like death trembling, and it comes throughout the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a candle made of goose fat, or a very strong vulture feather, and put this candle on the trembling, until the purple circle encloses the trembling all around; then turn your hand all around the candle, pressing all around the trembling, and push it deep down, and pull out the trembling by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a needle of bronze or iron according to this form, and let it be slender beneath and broad above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you wish, cauterize the wound, as it is before the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or brass, or molten copper or lead; and sometimes it is made with these small and large instruments, according to which they are made for someone.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are administered treatment for children and those who are feeble and in pain are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is above wide, where the bellies are tied according to this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a detachment where the belly is tied, as you see, and the anus is inside, pierced; and it has two openings on one side, and one on the other; and the belly is like a bag in which one puts medicines made of a beast's bladder or parchment, pierced all around with small holes, with an inch of space between each hole, then weave a strong thread wound around in an X or in a spiral all around, and assemble the belly so that it is like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, attach it to the instrument with a strong thread, then enema; and this is the shape of the ring:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or egg white, or a similar substance, then insert it gently; then the minister squeezes his two hands together, as much as he can, then pull out the syringe, and let the patient lie on his side, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him hold it in as long as he can; and if he sleeps for a night, that is a great help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema him for an illness of diarrhea, and the medicine wants to come out quickly, do it again until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the rectum or anus, let the syringe be as fine as for a child; and that is the way to make the thin syringe that pulls the skin:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the cure of wounds; now we will tell you about the cures with hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and depending on the location and the cause of the wound.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the impact of a stone, and cutting with a sword or knife, or lance, or staff, or arrow, or similar objects; or they are made according to the places in the body, such as a wound that bleeds from the neck, or head, or leg, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, one should take care if it is from a stone or similar object, and the skin is still broken and the wound is large, and you quickly doubt a hot abscess: then make it bleed with the cephalic vein immediately if there is a little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be in the opposite direction of the injured part; and let the patient avoid fullness of wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, then let his food be diminished, and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come out, cotton wet only in rose oil, or in strictive wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, as long as it has all its blood, and it has not been moved by the air, powder, which I will speak of shortly; and if the fire has moved it, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword-cut and similar, and the lips cannot be approximated with tenting, then approximate them with suturing, as I will say for abdominal wounds, from the ribs up.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, and it can be closed, and holds only by a little, then cover it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, as well as meat, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find pus in the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, then open it all the way, and let it drain out, then cure it; and if there is a vein in the wound or vein, which does not clot, and cannot be stanched by medicine, then tie off the vein, and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy: you should apply this powder that heals as soon as the burn occurs.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take one part incense; two parts dragon's blood; three parts quicklime, and mix the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly in place until it heals well and joins to all its blood; and then bind it up tightly, and leave it without loosening, if it is not swollen; for the medicine is not removed until it has healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes this from quicklime only, when one does not have the incense or dragon's blood, but the fire should open the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has been moved by the fire, let it be in the same state, and do not apply any of this powder to it; but apply some digestive ointments, or a poultice made from barley flour with water and honey, until it oozes; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if there is a fracture of bone with the wound, and it is small, I will extract it with delicate tweezers; and I will tell you about fractures of the skull later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and the one on the head, except that the nerves or arteries of the neck are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, there is nothing else to do but leave the wound untreated and apply no restraining agent, for it harms the nerves and makes them withdraw; and apply nothing cold to the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation within is with the brain, which is the highest member; but use warm remedies, such as a wash in lukewarm water, and mixed with rose oil, and cooked wash also in lukewarm water, and other minerals according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then cut it and ligature it, and then treat it until it is healed.Et si li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is chapped and full of pus, then pierce it or a lower place; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding ensues, then ligate it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the passage for food is blocked, then cut the windpipe above the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then bind it firmly, and leave it for several days, then treat with ointments that promote sloughing until it is healed; and if the wound has affected the bone, then trepan it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them all if you can, and those you cannot reach, then leave them until the wound granulates and the wound is closed; and if the wound is fresh, then apply the powder I described earlier.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a stab wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then examine whether blood issues from the wound except for wind-like breath: then you know that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put the powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it up because of the blood that seeps out, but let it return to the body, and heal the patient. But apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you do not have an ointment, then place old cotton in the wound to soak up moisture, and let the patient sleep with his head on the wound for three, or four, or more days; then no spasms, nor bad tremors of the body, nor strangulations of breath will come. And when you see good signs, then you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it therefore with poultices and other remedies until it is healed; and if it will not heal, and keeps weeping, then know that there is a fistula; treat it then as it should be treated.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, in the front or back, treat it as we have said before; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, powder it, and if it has bitten into the bone, and there are pieces loose, then clean out the wound, and draw out the pieces if they are loose; and for other wounds in other limbs, judge as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	There are great, medium, and small ruptures of the belly; from a large wound sometimes the intestine or the nerves of the intestines protrude, by which there is an entrance for air; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because when one sews up the intestines little by little, they swell as soon as they feel the cold, so that they are more easily sewn little by little; and thus it is better to treat a smaller wound, because one sews up the intestine gradually to its place rather than all at once. And know that there are four kinds of ruptures of the belly: two kinds of common suturing occur in the suturing of the belly, and two other kinds of proper suturing are common to other wounds; and yet they are more proper for the suturing of the belly, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something from the intestines has come out, and a greased cloth is used to push it back in, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or soft cloth in lukewarm water, or cook it in squinant and cypress and spurge, and apply the intestines until the swelling is reduced; and sometimes this wine-based compress helps, and it is necessary to use it repeatedly to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subsiding, moisten the intestines with water or warm tea made from mallows, because a little constriction causes the entrance to close slightly; and if it cannot be pushed in, make a small incision in the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is better than cutting, which should only be done in case of great necessity; and the instrument for splitting it is described as follows: cut into the curve and remove it, and see the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines leap out, then put them back in according to their natural shape in their proper place, if you have the power, for this is best.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is low on the belly, you should make the patient lie on his back with his legs above his head; and if it is high up, then put the head and feet higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture is on one side, then have the wounded part highest. And thus you should arrange things as I say, in both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;
