puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what you have available, then take a needle in your hand and press the edges of the wound together; this is the common method of suturing, and it involves piercing both sides of the skin and the subcutaneous tissue underneath with one or more needles, depending on the size of the wound, leaving a small gap at the top, then passing the needle through all four edges of the wound, pulling them together; then tie off the thread around the needle, and repeat this process according to how many needles you need, ensuring they are not too deep in the flesh or skin, so as not to reopen the wound; then tie off the threads so that they do not bother the patient when sleeping, and place tents or bandages over the needles to keep them in place until the wound heals. This method of suturing with needles is best for small wounds, as a larger one will require a different approach: take a needle and thread, pierce all four edges of the wound, pulling them together; then bring the needle back to where you started, in the manner of sewing a garment, leaving a gap between each stitch equal to half a finger's width; this method healed a man who had been stabbed in the belly, with his intestines hanging out, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and the intestines protruded by more than two palms.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his intestines after they had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up for 15 days, and I treated it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I didn't treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where there was neither ointment nor medicine; and I put old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle and insert it from the outside through to the inside; when it has pierced right through from one side to the other, hold the thread at the exit point where you inserted the needle, and pierce through from the other side of the wound to the outside; the understanding of this sewing is that you sew just as the furriers do furs, and you leave one end of the thread on one side, and pick it up on the other, so that the sewing is completed all around.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen describes correctly, is as follows: take two pieces of skin and join them together naturally, applying one edge of the flap to the other, like so: insert a needle into the proximal edge of the flap, and pierce only that spot, leaving the two edges of the flap; then turn the needle and pierce from the outside in, through both edges of the flap, until you reach the inside; next, pierce one and then the other side of the flap from the outside in, through two other edges of the skin that are on the opposite side; this is the most common and proper method of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this, and some testify to it: one should sew the abdomen with two needles, with thread in each; and one should push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and know that when the incision is on the abdomen, the suturing is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are like the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound all its blood, as long as the burn has moved, it puts back the bowels, and the envelope; then put on the powder char, and if the burn has moved, put on some ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and cut the thread, and sew up the edges, and the mirror; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicine, as soon as it begins to heal, place old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will cause community to the principal members, then you should moisten a light cloth in tempered warm oil, or in rose oil, and place it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if there is pain or swelling in the bowels, which often happens, then enema with warm black wine, and likewise if the swelling comes up to the intestines; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines, which are called "young," cannot heal when they are raw, and this is due to the thinness of the veins that they are made of, and the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of their nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the gallbladder pops out of the wound, put it back in like the intestines, as long as it's fresh; but if it's old and has become green or black, you should tie off the area that is black so that no blood flow comes from it, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut away what is between the ligature, and hang the two ends of the wound down to drain and facilitate extraction when the gallbladder breaks, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the thread
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are ruptured, and the wound is small, one can sometimes restore it in some people, for I saw a man who was pierced in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and from it came digestion and flatulence; I applied a cautery according to what I could, and did not cease to cauterize until he was healed, and the wounds closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewing, I doubted that the patient had a problem in his belly; and he had no harm, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in such a way: take a thread from a great testicle, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened the mouth, put it on both lips so that it tightens his mouth; and then he covers the head, and it is held so that it cannot come undone, then put another thread after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and heal the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If these wounds are in the intestines and no harm comes to the patient, one can sew up the intestines with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in the following way: take the end of this intestinal thread that is very thin, then tie it to the end of a fine linen thread which is twisted, then put the thread through the needle and sew up the wound, and tie it in the opening; and this method of sewing with threads is nothing other than according to the way of hope and expectation; and if the wound is large and broad, especially when it is in one of the intestines, there is no healing or health, except by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula, wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and becomes pus-filled.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the green node, formed from a hard and white growth, where there is no pain, and it is as swollen as the beak of a bird; sometimes it is clear and pus-filled, and sometimes thick; sometimes small, and sometimes large; I have already spoken about these in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no scabs, is only due to one of nine causes: namely, due to the smallness of blood or body fluids; or because of its malignancy; or because there is a hard mass within it, and on the surface, that does not allow pus to form; or because there is too much inflammation; or the location is swollen, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine used for treatment is ineffective; or the corruption is of a pestilential nature; or due to the natural characteristics of the region, digestion and healing are slow, and swelling occurs. Or there may be veins or bones involved: I have already described all these causes, their signs, and the medicinal cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you about the treatment for a fistula that is performed manually.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas can occur in any part of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins and arteries and nerves, or from the sinus, or intestine, or bladder, or any of the ribs, or from the spine in the back, or from any joint in the hands or feet; and they can affect the primary function of a limb, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this way are painful to heal, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is a fistula that does not come to the places I have described, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it working, then take an iron or bronze tent, if the fistula is straight, then pierce it; and if the fistula is crooked, then probe with a thin, flexible rod of lead, for the lead bends with the crookiness. And if there are several openings in the fistula and you cannot probe it well with tents, then cleanse it by enema through one of the openings, for moisture will flow from one opening to another, and cleanse it; then pierce it gently as you can, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and feel how deep it goes; and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and where he feels it; and when you know for sure where it is located, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or any of the places I have mentioned to you, then treat it as I have instructed, and remove the foulness and rotten matter inside. Then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep and straight, then you should probe deeply, as much as you can, then apply moist tents with medicinal water, and let them sit at the mouth of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes away the excess matter at the bottom; then apply healing ointments to cleanse the wound, until it is healed. If it is not healed by this method, then cauterize as we have described, and if the bone is rotten with the fistula, then treat it likewise.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve in your limbs is not causing you grief, as we have said, and if there is decay and blackness in the bone, then treat it with a poultice until it is healed; and if it is not healed and swells again as before, know that you have not gone deep enough: probe and dig until you reach the bottom, and remove all the decay, then restore the joint; and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the decay is too deep for you to reach it; then do nothing but let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupt bone, and you can pull it out with tweezers, or with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, one by one; and if moisture causes a contrary effect, and there is no error or fear, then cut and dry, and use poultices, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, then place something on the wound to cause swelling, and let it swell around the bones, and then they will become looser; and if it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, then cleanse only the rottenness until all the darkness is removed, and then heal the wound. And if there is a great deal of decay, and it comes down to the soft tissue of the bone, then it should be lanced and covered all the way to the decay, and then healed as it grows together. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take an example and aid from this in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from inside the body, so that the matter came out to the leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but the doctors, through their folly, operated on it until the abscess opened, and a lot of matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many holes opened through which the body fluids flowed; and many doctors treated him for two years without any wisdom in the art of medicine, so that I was called to treat him. When I saw his leg and the medicines that were used on him, and what flowed from the holes into the body, it was a great illness; and the young man's skin turned red, and he had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent at one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one came up against another throughout the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried therefore, and probed one of the openings until I exposed a portion of the bone, and found it rotten and piercing through, and the corruption extended to the bone within; I treated what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and thought there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and then began to heal the wound with strong medicines for a long time, but could not close it; so I began again, and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and treated it, and then removed it, and strove hard to close the wound; but was unable to do more than probe around a palm's breadth of the bone, and drew it out entirely from its socket, and then healed it with medicines; and it was cured quickly, and there was no need to resume the operation except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often due to the bloodletting he bled profusely, but he was completely healed, and in the bone a hard lump grew, and he had a good disposition and had no harm or contrary effect at all, neither when lying down nor when rising.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, it should be bound in this way: take a bandage, and tie it to the head of the exposed bone, and instruct someone to pull it upwards; and place another larger woolen bandage over the hard lump on top of the bone, and hold the end, so that you draw the corrupted flesh towards the bottom, and uncover the flesh above where you want to bind it, so that the bandage does not stick to the flesh; and place a hot coal or a flat stone underneath the bone to cover the corrupted flesh; and one should keep binding as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and bind again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the bone is broken and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in part, then uncover the flesh all around; then place a fire underneath, and then cut from one side of the corruption to the other, and cut the healthy bone away from the corruption as far as it goes, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut through the corrupted joint and cut the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no need to cut further than the joint; and if the corruption is at the knuckle of the hand or the foot, it is a very serious matter, but you must still investigate the corrosion and how it appears to you; cleanse it in every way you can, as long as the vein or nerve does not cause you any trouble; and know that there are many ways to cut these bones, depending on the position of the bones, their appearance, their thickness and thinness, their size and smallness, and their hardness. And so you must prepare an instrument for each type of task; and know that your work will show you the instrument you need, according to your knowledge of this art and the characteristics of the diseases; then choose the instrument you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head can suffer damage due to internal causes or external; and when you have treated this corrosion with medicine, if it does not help, then you must cover the affected limb up to where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient escapes death by this poison or by the greater evil of losing the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if burned by fire, and after the blackness appears, the corrosion spreads from limb to limb throughout the body. If it is caused by the sting of some venomous creature, such as a scorpion or snake, and the sting is on the head, then cover it and do not give it any opportunity to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, cover it at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cover it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy but to cut off the limb according to its size; and thus do with the leg also: if it reaches the first joint, cover it after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, cover all of it; and if it goes up into the leg, cover at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to cut off the limb, or the patient will die. The way to cover the limb with a bandage is to tie it above and below, and extend one instrument down from one of the ties, and another instrument up from the other tie, and open the flesh between the two ties with a broad spatula, so that the bone is exposed; then cover it and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the bandage does not touch the healthy part, and bring the patient more injury and abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the area gently or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete, then tie the injured limb with a suitable ligature and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man one night: he had a dark discoloration that looked like a burn, and this corrosion began at the toe of his foot, spreading to cover the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he bandaged his foot, and it healed. And long after, the corrosion appeared on the finger of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied repulsive substances after cleansing his body, but I could not stop the corrosions; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I refused, for I had no hope that the material would be repelled; and I feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's vitality was weak. And he despaired completely, returned to his homeland, bandaged his hand, and healed; and I have never heard of this method being used except in this case, should anyone need it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	There are times when an abscess forms in a fleshy area and remains for so long that it causes a great gathering of pus; then it ruptures and pierces, and the pus flows out, leaving a hollow space beneath the skin, just like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as a piece of cloth, and does not heal all the way to the bone or nerve, and such a condition is called a 'sore' and not a 'fistula'; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone, then it is called a 'fistula', and you can see right through the skin all around it, just like through a piece of cloth; and it does not heal because of its infection.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have reason to believe that the skin is healing and the infection is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it thus: examine whether the abscess is large and the pus within has a foul odor; then prepare an Egyptian medicine as follows: take equal parts of alum, oil, and litharge, and melt them together in a vessel over fire until the mixture turns red and thickens like honey; then take some of this according to your need, and dilute it with water and honey, and inject it into the abscess, and allow it to remain for two hours before squeezing it out; repeat this several times until the abscess is completely cleaned and healed, and the pus is removed; and if you do not have the Egyptian medicine at hand, then prepare a clister of ashes from grapevines: gather some ashes and pour water over them, then strain the liquid and use it to inject into the abscess until you see that it is cleansed; and if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then use a mixture of water and honey with a little litargire ground into it; or inject a mixture of honey and wine, letting the honey work to cleanse and the wine to dry up the sore; and once this is done and you see that the abscess is cleansed, then inject something that encourages flesh growth inside it: prepare an emulsion of diaphoretic powder with rose oil and wine; or inject some medicinal ointments, as I have described in the section on ointments; and if the opening of the abscess is small and the tube of the clister cannot enter, then enlarge it with a needle and apply a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged enough for the clister to enter; and if the wound is too large, then cut away only as much as is necessary for the clister to reach the affected area, and if the opening that drains the pus is above, then apply the tent lower down.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Because when the bowels are full, you should not let any charioting ensue; and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then prepare in such a way that the bowels move to the lowest place they can, for when the bowels are full, you should not let any charioting ensue, and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then prepare in such a way: that the bowels move slightly downward, and leave nothing of the bowels; and take consolidating medicines to put over the wound, and be above the linen drape that covers the entire wound; then cover the opening of the breast more widely than before, then apply ointment on the other drape according to the quantity of the opening, and place it on the opening of the wound to draw out the bowels, and do not remove the large drape except after several days once; and that which is over the opening of the breast, remove often to draw out the bowels, and know what comes from the bowels, whether it is venom or pus or enough or digestible or indigestible; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that rises on the opening of the wound, then know that the breast is healing, and approach the saints; and then loosen it in the morning, or the middle of the day, and when you loosen the wound, change the other drape, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if milk flows from the breasts for many days, know that the breast is not averted.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons spread over a long time, do not despair of your health, for health is drawing near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	Because there are some people in whose wounds putrid flesh slowly develops, and others who develop the opposite; and if digested humors shoot from the breast after many days, know that it is not healing; and if the breast is slow to heal and far away, apply dry medicines moist in substance but dry in virtue, such as a diaphenous ointment, because there is a large part of vitriol in it, and this is the final medicine; take a diaphenous ointment, and make it with rose oil, and rose water equal in substance; then cook it down and use it; and you can also cook honey thickened with sugar when diaphenous ointments are not available, or take myrrh, aloes and incense, powder them, and spread them on the honey that I mentioned above; and if the fistula is slow to heal and does not heal with this treatment, know that the corruption has gone deep, causing an impression in the bone, or a hard spot in the limbs or viscera; then follow the fistula cure we have described earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaris is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally in other places; and when it becomes infected, and no attention is paid to it, then the abscess becomes deep, and it runs and oozes pus as far as the root of the nail, and sometimes all the way around; and corrosion extends to the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the part swells, and the color turns yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the section, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the dead tissue that remains beneath the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cautery is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy; and if the nail grows into the flesh, and begins to grow out, and the blisters, then you must put a wire under the nail so that it pulls the flesh away, and draw it upward, and carefully cut away the dead flesh, and apply ardant and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then treat with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and pull it out, for as long as the bone remains corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see that it is about to become corrupted, cut it in front of the knuckle as before described, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is swollen and pained, then you must first treat it; next, cut the nail of the sprain diagonally from above, taking care not to cut down to the flesh beneath the nail, for otherwise the patient would feel great pain; and if this happens, place something on top to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the shoulder
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The nails of some people's hands grow out curved, and sometimes they have bones in them, and occasionally a claw, and in others the nail grows from the root of the joint, or from one of the knuckles.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in the navel of the eye does not move, and he who is born at the junction of the eye sometimes moves; the size of him who is fleshy is thus light, in such a way: cut it at its root with a broad spatule.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who was born in the root of the joint is painful to cure: you must hold the cupping.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For him who is born in the back of the eye, you must first cut the flesh around the socket, then cut the bone with a convenient silk to that, then clean it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come by birth, or by wound, or by burn, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Then you must cut the socket so that the eye can fit back in according to their natural shapes; then put between two tents or moistened sheets in rose oil, so that they do not adhere; or put between two pieces of subtle plaster, until the sockets are adherent, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If it comes to one of his hands with the palm, then sew up that wound as it should be.
des vils	of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large enveloped vessels filled with melancholy superfluities, which come in many parts of the body; and they occur more in legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.Et avient plusors foiz en veine perroniere, et en celle que l’on appelle artere, qui est de contree la veine sus la cheville de la jambe, ains qu’elle ne soit en leus naturelz; et plus avient a cele perroniere qu’a l’artere.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him some purgative medicine, and then the basil oil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with fire has two methods: one is to cauterize the veins and draw out the black blood; the other method is to open a vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The procedure for the incision is as follows: first, place a hot water compress on the leg until the large veins are dilated, then stretch out the leg from above the thigh to the area below the knee; then cut an incision in one place, or two or three places, with a broad cut, then open and draw out the black blood by hand from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can tolerate without harm; then ligate it, and order that he eat meat mixed with black bile; and resume the evacuation and bleeding when the incisions have healed, and repeat as necessary.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the joint is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in the bath, and pour hot water on the leg until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over the fire, and then cut the skin at the vein near the knee or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin around the vein, and scrape the vein from each side until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then tie it beneath with thread, so that it is raised from the skin, and then cut it gently at the knuckle, then cut another slit, or more if you need to, then lift and cut at the toe, then pull and lift up to the second slit; then draw it out from slit to slit until it is all out, then cut it off; and if you cannot pull and raise it, then tie a strong double thread to an awl, and pierce and pull it, and tie it beneath the vein, and turn your hand from side to side so that it comes out; and be careful that it does not tear, for if it tears, then one cannot pull and raise it, and harm comes to the patient; and when you have treated it all, then place soft wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the wound site, and treat it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cut it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron used to split the vein is curved and does not cut so that it does not cut the vein; and it is a large curve because if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but it should be large as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the legs, in hot areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in land with no moisture; and sometimes it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from porridge that comes under the skin, as snakes and worms do, lurking between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes a great inflammation in the leg, then change the place, and begin the vein going out, just as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder opens, you should wrap around a piece of plaster from three and a half to four inches, and tie it, and leave the plaster hanging on the leg, and every time that there is no point in the wound, then wrap around the plaster, and tie it; and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap the rest, and do not cover it at its root as long as it is all coming out; for if you cover it, then it goes into the flesh, and makes an abscess and pus in the place, and a bad disease; because of this thing, it should be treated little by little to the head, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein is when it is treated from five or ten palms long, and a man came to me, to whom it came out ten palms long, and when you cover it, then plug one hole or opening, and pierce it to the bottom so that all comes out; and empty the matter which is inside, and bring medicine to the place on swelling some days, then cure it as the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein bleeds profusely, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and a lot of pus comes out, and from which it rains; therefore treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that arise between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "disease of oxen" in our land because it often affects oxen. It is a small worm that arises between skin and flesh and moves throughout the body, ascending and descending, until it erupts through the skin where it travels, and jumps out. It is caused by putrid humors, just like worms, snakes, and earthworms in the belly. It is feared for its malice, because when it moves through the body and ascends to the head, it can enter and destroy the eye, which often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and pulled out, one cannot help but cry out in pain when he sees it; therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a strong string tightly, then press down on it and pull it out forcefully; if the blood runs profusely into the flesh, and you cannot stop it, cauterize it with fire until it stops bleeding. The greatest harm that can occur is that it will affect the eye, as we have said before; therefore, if you see it coming close to the eye, press underneath it firmly, then pull it out; you must use remedies that cleanse the body of infectious humors and meat that promotes putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vomiting" in our land, and it is a pain that occurs in some parts of the body and then moves from one part to another; I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and uncovered her arm, and saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm; and a little later, I saw it rising up like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, as bright as silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later ran through the whole body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that she was turning around in the body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never before seen this disease progress in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I have seen many whose pain moved from one place to another, but I did not see it in the woman; and I thought that it was because women have dry bodies, and their veins are uncovered, and thus appears this compelled windiness; and they do not appear in this way to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to treat this disease, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then tie it above and below tightly, and then press on it until that windiness is forced out of its place; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it yourself, then have it treated by someone who dispels windiness, such as with foul pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	There are many types of stones, some with large points, small, smooth, and pointed; and some with two angles, and some with tongues, and some are hollow; and they can break in a limb in two ways: either in a principal member like the brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, kidney, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she falls, therefore, in any part of these members, and the sign of death which I shall tell you about afterwards becomes apparent, then you must be wary of extracting this arrow; for death follows upon many dispositions; and when this evil sign is not apparent to you, and the arrow is not deeply imbedded, draw it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow pierces and penetrates the bone, and the membrane which covers the brain, is seen to be cut, and blood and pus flow out, and a swelling and redness appear in them, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of blood; and perhaps also mucus flows from the nose or ears; and perhaps also they lose their speech and voice; and there issue from the wound white moisture resembling pus, and also a bruise-like discoloration; and if these signs appear to you, cease your treatment, and extract the arrow if it is not deeply imbedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of a hernia when it occurs in the chest are that it is located near the left breast, and feels as if it were lodged in a hard object, not soft; and sometimes the hernia is silent like the pulse, and emits black blood, and there is a chill and cold sweat, and syncope: then know without a doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the wound that never leave the chest are foam-filled bile coming from the wound, and a swollen throat, and the patient's colour changing, and high panting, and chilliness leaving.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces the sole of the foot, it affects the small bones; and causes great swelling and great pain and sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulder are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, by chance something indigestible might jump out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces the belly, and nothing comes out through the rectum but feces, then there is little hope for a cure or for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, and urine comes out and escapes, and the patient feels great pain: know that this wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, spine of the back, forearm, thigh, and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow hit him in the jaw at its root near the nose; I treated it, and pulled it out from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without bleeding.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I treated an arrow that had hit him in the fat of the eye under the eyelid, and the arrow was lodged there, and only its tip was protruding towards the nose; the arrow was as long as a Turkish bowstring, with a light iron tip, and the man was healed without any bad consequences.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I removed an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears; I cut the beards, and I removed it gently until it came out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I removed an arrow from a man's home, which was lodged in his stomach, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not improve; I cut above the arrow, and I probed it, and pulled it out, and he had no bad reaction.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man with an arrow lodged in his back, and the wound is sewn up on top; and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions are not changed, and he finds no harm in any of his natural actions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man who had an arrow in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and he remained like that without experiencing great pain; and many others similarly.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow wound in the home of the prince the king, who had a wound in his head, and was slightly tilted to the right; and the arrow was lodged completely. I was called to tend to it after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with a thin instrument, and did not feel anything; but he felt piercing and pain underneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed an astringent and digestive poultice on the site to prevent swelling; and the location of the arrow became apparent to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice again the next day, and the wound healed quickly; but the patient felt the arrow inside his nose for a long time, and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a strong corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open and I probed it, feeling the head of the arrow that had pierced through; then, by means of this medicine, I cleared away the obstruction in the wound until the head of the arrow became visible; and the patient made a full recovery within four months. Then I cleansed the wound and, using tweezers, pulled out the arrowhead; but it would not come out, so I continued to work on it with various instruments until one day I was able to extract it with specially made tweezers, as described in this chapter, and thus healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they thought that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; so I restored it, and the wound healed up, and the patient made a full recovery.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you place your treatment on what I do not say, because books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters reason well about very few things, and about what is present and lacking to them, they devise new works and new instruments, from the descent of strange things that come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows strike the members where they are pierced in two ways: either through the place where they enter or through another part; and those that exit through the place where they entered are arrows entering into fleshy parts, and sometimes they exit now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not exit now, then leave it as long as the flesh around it becomes putrid and the outlet is cleared; and also if it is pierced into the bone and cannot exit, then leave it for a few days, and move it every day; and then it will exit, and if it does not, then pierce through to the very tip of the arrow, making the hole around it wider, and then pull it out.
