Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull, and goes just to one of the brains, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: then do not pull it out, but let it be until it is equalized after some days, for if the arrow comes to the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not lodged in the bone only, and does not come to the brain, and the patient remains for some days without a bad accident, then prepare the engine to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is lodged very deeply and cannot be removed, then administer bleeding around the wound, as I have told you; then clean the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in a place in the body where it cannot be seen, it should be sought throughout the body; and if it can be felt, pull it out with any convenient instrument; and if due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow there is no bone or nerve or vein, then cut it as much as the wound is large; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears by which it holds in the arrow, remove the flesh that is lodged on both sides as far as you can, and then break or fold the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; be careful not to break the arrow as you pull it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then leave it until around the nail it becomes soft, then pull it out, for its extraction is easy.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the bleeding makes you feel faint, then do as we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of cutting into the nerve and opening a vein, and use the means by which you can best pull out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to how he was when the arrow struck him, for that is the greatest help, and if you cannot do that, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Arrows that come from elsewhere, or where something of it is visible, or the skin is swollen at that spot so that one can see or feel it: cut there, as far as the pincers can reach, and then pull it out; if it will not come out just now, try again later.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, rotate your hand around, as far as it goes into the bone, and widen the hole, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot be extracted, then leave it for now and try again later; if there is still some of the arrow inside, then remove all of its shaft; if part of the arrow is broken off, and you can use a tool to grab it, then place the tip of the tool so that it enters the arrow's head; then pull it out, and if the arrowhead is lodged in the tool, then pull it out with the arrow.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces the shoulder or the chest or belly or bladder or ribs, and it is deep, and you can cut around it, then do so; but be careful not to cut into the vein and nerve, and then pull it out, and then sutured the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird; see the illustration:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many varieties: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the head of the arrow is like the feather of a bird, to push towards the tip of the arrow, just as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of tweezers for pushing and gripping is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one recovers, and they have XVI branches in the head, namely: II veins which are behind the ears, called the "two ear-veins"; and the II arteries which are in the II temples, visible; and II veins that are in the II corners of the II eyes, called "aspiring veins"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two windpipes which are in the neck; and the II veins that are above the lips, and these are the veins called "age-veins"; and the II veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which we commonly heal are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side of the chest, and the common people call it 'vein of the head'; and the middle one is called 'fast', and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the common people call it 'vein of the heart'; and the basilic is on the right side of the chest, and the common people call it 'vein of the belly', and it is above the femoral, and is that from which we heal, which opens clearly above the groin.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvator is the vein between the auricular and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and the foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the groin on the left side of the chest, and the second is sophene, which is at the ankle on the right side of the chest; and the vein called 'nesse', which is at the ankle on the other side.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of veins that are behind the ears is helped by old catarrhs and by emigraine; and the qualities of the bleeder, as I told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then compress the patient's neck with a bandage so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head; then press them with your fingers, and where you feel the pulse under your fingers, sign there; then take the lance, and pierce under the vein all the way to the bone, then lift your hand over the entire vein upstream, and stab through the skin and the vein well twice with the lance, and make the blood come out; then compress and ligate it until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is useful for old migraines, and for headaches, and for habitual blindness, and for ague in the eyes; and the quality of the bleeder is as I have said: and it is that the patient holds his neck still, so that the two veins are clearly visible; and feels the pulse under your thumb, and then sign with your finger; then lift the vein at the top of your index finger, and insert the lance underneath, and lift the vein at the top, and bandage it, as you did with the other veins; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their binding and their release in the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding from the vein in the forehead is as good as the bleeding from the cephalic vein for old diseases of the face, and for emigration and redness; and the qualities are such that the patient turns his neck in twisting until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, and apply pressure with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the amount you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and sometimes the wound is closed with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too sharp; and ligate the vein crookedly, for the bone is near, and by chance the flames may break when they are delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding from the two veins that are in the jaw helps with teeth, and with tinea, and with redness, and with a growth on the eye, and with diseases of the face; and the qualities of their bleeding are such that the patient turns his neck by twisting some ligament, as before; then he bleeds, and the bleeding is through the skin, a little from the long flame a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are thin, they may break; then stop the bleeding, as much as you need to, and then bind it with a linen bandage, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein in the nose is good for ague, and for sudden madness, and for diseases of the face, such as migrainous headache and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is chronic; and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient should hold his neck back, then squeeze his nose with his left hand, take a long, thin flame, and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well otherwise, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then ligate it overnight, for it is quickly restored; and this is the way of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two blood vessels also helps with strangulation of the windpipe, and with the beginning of hoarseness, and with many diseases, and with phlegmon, and with ulcers, and with herpes, and with eye diseases; and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient should hold his neck back as we have said; and let the operator stand above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then bleed the vein on the side a little widely, then draw the blood gently, or as much as is needed; then do the same on the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and squeeze both veins gently so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding from the gums
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The salves for sores on the lips above also help with ulcers in the mouth, and gum decay, and lip splits, and inner and outer lips.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the bleeding is to have the patient sit in front of you and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they can be recognized because they are black, and because there are small black veins around them: therefore press one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you doubt which they are, then press the largest of each side, and likewise do to the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The healing of veins that are under the tongue is helped by the healing of the cephalic vein, and it is in the constriction of the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and in diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the vein-healer is such that the patient should hold their hand in front of the sun, and touch the tongue, and look underneath on each side for a black vein: heal both of them, and do not go too deep, because there are arteries underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly healed are healed in two ways: either by pricking with a large mirtin flame, or an olive-shaped subtile needle called "anesil"; and they are large and subtile according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame of the myrtle is very famous, and is wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the flat veins of the neck that contain gross and troubled blood; and this is the shape of the olive-shaped flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for bleeding the veins gently, where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses under the throat, in the neck, in the chest, and in the abdomen; and the surgeon must cauterize bleeding and guard against the artery underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If it pierces the artery and bleeding occurs, then it must be stanched as I have said; and the flame should not be held firmly but gently touched like a needle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the basilic does not open clearly, then you must stretch it and change to another vein; or you may want some of its branches, or cauterize the vein in the arm where it opens clearly; and hold the flame gently, as we have said.Et s’il appert, si covient qu’il estainche la voinne, et qu’il coppe au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit; et ne doit mie demorer en la voinne, mas le flamme fust ferme et estaincha la voinne, et qu’il se vaueille de l’artere.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the location of the bleeding, then you must stretch out the arm and touch the area until you feel the pulse; then sign the spot with your fingernail, and then tie up the arm, and stop the vein with flame quickly; and be careful not to pierce the artery when you see the spot puffed up, for that is the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rising up like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery: act quickly therefore, and place your finger over it for a long time; then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens. Tie up the arm and leave it as it is, without moving it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and he faints and medicine is not present, then press on the artery above where it is cut and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of wood from an oak tree, split it in half and take one of the pieces and tie it on tightly until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then treat it with powders that stop bleeding, as we have said. And the stopping of the bleeding is not due to the size of the wound or the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bleeding from the vein is helped if it draws blood from the top of the head and from the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the surgeon must be careful not to pierce too deeply, and he should find the nerve beneath, and if it is swollen and the vessels are congested, and cannot heal, then this nerve often opens, and if it does not open in some men due to its subtlety, then you should cauterize it with a hot instrument; and cauterize the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is bleeding between the two nerves, they will make a long cut.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	Bleeding from the cephalic vein is helped if it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it should be cauterized with an olive-oil flame or a myrtle flame, for this is the safest of all veins because there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, one should seek the lightest method, and if one fails the first time, one should try again; and sometimes the site swells in some men when one fails the first time, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is only done to maintain health and prevent future illnesses; and bleeding should be performed in one of the three veins: the cephalic, the facial, and the basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of Lent, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of digestion are apparent; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bleeding that is administered for illnesses has no set time, but whenever there is a need, day or night, at any hour and at all times; and one should not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying a fetus beyond the fourth month until the seventh month.Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	They should not bleed those who are over sixty years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary that he purges the intestines with a gentle enema if he has a lot of retained feces, so that the veins do not attract harmful superfluities from the intestines into the principal limbs; nor should one bleed those who are too bloated from meat, or who are drunk, as long as they remain so, nor the hydropsy, and if anyone wants to bleed after colic pain, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent intercourse with a woman, and from labor, from waking and fasting, and from whatever weakens the body, either through weapons or from the body itself; then subtly withdraw the humors if the blood is thick, through meat and drink and medicine, if you have the power to do so; then enter the bath, if nothing else weakens him, to subtilize the blood, and he should be bled from the vein of the foot around midnight, as we have said; and he should guard himself that day from exertion, and from pain, and from luxury, and from similar things; and he should lie down and relax, and the bleeding person should be higher than the one being bled, and he should rub the arm two or three times, then gently tighten the bandage above the middle, for if it is too tight or too loose, it cannot draw the blood out; then he should rub the place with his hand until the veins swell and can be felt; then wet the bleeding person's hand with a little old oil, then put his thumb from his left hand on the vein under the place where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not shrink away from the blade.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flow like cords to the heart, and some that are filled with winds, so that when one applies flame, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus one finds these things; and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, so it is necessary for the surgeons to be skilled in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, try again a little lower at the same site or above it, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the part is swollen and the patient feels distressed, then let him wait for one or two days without binding the arm: perhaps a hot abscess will develop; and do not enter into a bath, then begin the bleeding again if it pleases her; and if the opening is small, then cut through the skin subtlely and you doubt that it will not flow as much blood as you wish, then apply the flame directly to that opening; and work gently, so that the part becomes swollen; because this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the area swollen, do not re-open the wound, and apply a little liniment of oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the liniment of oil is used; and in this way administer the liniment of oil in every wound that you open veins to stop the flow of blood; and this also makes a poultice and bandage when applied to the area; thus the blood flows gently and separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess forms, which often happens, especially when the wound is not bled except for the first time or when the opening of the vein is small, be quick and apply to the area a sponge moistened with warm water and salt, and hold it for an hour; and you should do this after the flow of blood from the wound, and if anything remains in the area after several days, a blackness or greenness, it does no harm; and if you see it, apply some aloe or myrrh made into a poultice, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and appearance at the bleeding of basil: place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft to the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore placing on it anything of what we have mentioned, for perhaps it cuts into an artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its amount and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for those who are full and swollen, and need bloodletting, that one makes them a larger wound, and the flames should be wide; and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and they should be bled little and often, and one should bleed them by cutting across, not puncturing; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is better than bleeding from a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for those whose body needs bleeding, one should give them moist bread in pomegranate juice; if they are hot-tempered, bleed them three or four times. And if of a cold complexion, eat moist bread before the bleeding in syrup made from mulled wine, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger and cloves, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he faints during bleeding, after the loss of a lot of blood, he should drink a warm drink and a subtle scented syrup, and use the other remedies we mentioned in the chapter on syncope, to open the veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to wound his arm and bleed again, as needed, when it is weakened by heavy bleeding, let him bleed a little at a time, according to the amount of his strength, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to wound his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed elsewhere, let him bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is a lot of blood in the body that has become heated and causes fever; therefore, you must draw out a large quantity and widen the opening so that it bleeds freely; then you should examine all the conditions of bleeding, and put your hand over his pulse when he bleeds, so that death does not come through the vein, and this happens many times when the bleeder is careless; and when you see the arm loosening and bleeding a second time, and the opening is closed, you must press firmly on it; nor if it is crooked, must you extend the arm suddenly, for that would be bad; but let it be as he bleeds a second time; or touch it with the tip of a flame, so that the congealed blood at the vein opening melts, and put a little cold water on it, and press lightly on it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and don't bind it, until the abscess is settled.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to let blood a second time, let it be in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are healed in place of the vein in the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of bleeding is for the patient to put their hand in hot water until the vein becomes red; then let it be bound gently so that the vein appears well, and then bleed now from the middle, not from the large or long vein; and let the incision be wide, and let the bleeding be done near the joint of the hand, and if blood does not come out, put the hand back in hot water and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is standing, do not put the hand back in hot water, because it is put more in winter than when standing; and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bleeding of the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: twist the hand, and put it in hot water until the vein swells, and if one sees it; and if you bleed from the middle, and if you cut it from top to bottom, it does no harm; and do not go too deep because the nerves are completely naked under the skin, and then put the hand back in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have stopped the bleeding as much as necessary, then put oil and silk on the wound to close it quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is useful for the disease of the mice, and do everything as I told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salvation of the soul is good for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the mind, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the bowels, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its salvation are that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the wound until it breaks, and lies on the joint of the foot; and if the wound is at the ankle, and up to the foot, they go very far into the bowels; therefore heal it at the widest vein, or at the ankle, which works better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you tie it on the foot, then be careful of the nerves that are underneath, and tie it across also as though cutting; and let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the healer fails the first time, they should try again a little higher up, for the place is salty; do not be afraid of nerves, as we have said, and likewise with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic nerve is at the back of the leg; its treatment is good for pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his healing is such that the patient enters the bath, and twists above the ankle IIII turns, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then heal in every way you can, and by crossing over; and it is better that you cover it, for the place is safe, and it is very relaxed in many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not believe it, then heal some vein of his which opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and make the blood flow as much as you can see, and then loosen the bandage, and put cotton on top and tighten it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Of cupping treatments:
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and bleeding is done in two ways: by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done by burning is in two ways: with all fire, or without fire; and cupping that is done by burning and by bloodletting is done at 14 places on the body, of which one is entirely at the top of the head; and the other is in the neck; and II others are on either side of the neck; and the cupping under the chin; and the cupping on the two shoulders; and the cupping over the hips; and the cupping among the two arms; and the cupping of the two legs; and the cupping of the two ankles; and the cupping is not to be administered, neither with all fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	If for the sake of necessity or habit, one must bleed every hour at the beginning or end of the month, in the morning and evening and throughout the day. For there are some who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head; and some who experience bloating and redness on their face, head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, swollen tongue, and bleeding gums; and there are those who faint, and see dark things, wounds, and dead people.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the month of May, we order him to fast for three hours after daybreak.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with headaches ... that affect the eyes, and it must not be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this venting is in place of the bleeding of the head, and it must not be used by those who have a cold complexion, or who have catarrh, because it does them great harm; and for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often recover from it become obese, and for this reason, the cupping glasses should be placed a little lower due to the risk of obesity.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventouse on the neck is placed at the junction of the head and the base of the skull, and for this reason it helps with constrictions in the feet, and splits in the channel of the lungs, and with fullness, and repletion; and it should not be applied too strongly, for if it is held too tightly, it can cause obstruction or damage to the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventouse at the two sides of the neck helps with headache, and blindness and eye pain, and strangulation, and toothache, and is placed at the junction of the head and the base of the skull; and you must instruct the operator to express his hand when placing it so that he does not press the artery and cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation below the chin is good for mouth diseases, and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are worth a disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventouse on the sides of the chest is worth as much as three veins in the arm, for it draws blood from these large vessels; and instruct the operator not to press too deeply, for beneath there are nerves and arteries.Li ventosations dou bossu de la speche si vaut a dolors del petis, et est en leu de la sainie de la speche, et covient que li sainor la mette sus la speche et adentres, et non pas sur le col ou la gorge.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass which is on the buttock is good for varicose veins and for diseases underneath, and it must be a large cup made of brass, which needs to be applied with great care; and if it were too thin, it would break, causing large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs heal quickly because they draw blood from throughout the body and are good for old pains in the bones and joints, and the bladder, and restore the flow of fluids; they are located at the sides of the two knees and ankles, and over time they weaken the body and bring about fainting in many cases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping glass is that you first apply it empty, and suck gently, and place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area become red and swollen, and the blood vessel appear; then release, and re-apply the cupping glasses, and be mindful of the condition of the body, for there are those who have very sensitive skin, and small pores: so one should suck only once, and make wide wounds, and a little deep ones; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, one should suck twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it must be pricked three times; and when we want to draw a little blood, we prick only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we must bleed often; and if the blood is thick, then pierce it with a needle, and let the ends be so that the skin is pierced suddenly, and it suits those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, to anoint the places on the cupping glasses with aperitif and dissolutive oil: if it is in summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, use watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the surplus is large and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one to whom we bleed has soft skin and large pores, then no oil should be put on him, but he should be washed after bleeding with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from their bed, or from water of myrrh, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those with large superfluities rise from old wine, or from dry water, or from the decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not appropriate to bleed by leech before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and do not sleep after venting, and it is necessary that he be vigilant when he must be bled and when he is bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch if the person who is being bled is constipated, and if the blood is too thin and inflamed; then he should eat cool things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce with garlic, and similar things; and drink little, and eat the meat of young pigs, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold complexion should drink honey syrup, and moderate old and new scented wine, and drink little, and eat young pigs and pigeons; and the day he is bled, he should drink more than he eats; and it is appropriate to give some men theriac or musk before bleeding, or afterwards, to comfort the main limbs; and it should be subtle for the blood, but those with a hot complexion should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are put on without burning are those that are placed over the liver, and the mumps, and gout, and over the stomach and abdomen, and the kidneys and hips; because these members do not bear being burned under the eyes, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we do when we put them on the breasts when the child is teething; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we do when we apply cupping glasses over the stomach and abdomen to reduce the member; and it relieves pain when there is congestion or a stone, and by its attractive virtue it may draw out the congestion or force the stone from its place; and so it does when it is placed over the liver and the mumps when there is retained flatulence, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this way one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has a diameter of two inches and a half inch deep, and on the side near the middle there is a small hole, just large enough to push through a needle, and it should be made of brass, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a bar made of brass or iron, for placing a candle, and they come in both large and small sizes depending on the illness and age of those who use them; for the ventouses used by children are different from those used by the elderly, and those used by the thin are different from those used by the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this ventouse on the limb thus: take a candle of wax or tallow, and place it inside the ventouse through the bar in the middle, so that the flame is at the bottom of the ventouse and does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, and hold your fingers over the hole we mentioned, so that when you wish, the vapors can escape, and remove the ventouse; then apply the tallow as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered for disease of pleurisy, for all acute diseases, there is no pipe or aperture, and it is not removed until it is filled with water, and is placed on the limb only thus; and that is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are not removed until in members where one cannot place cupping glasses due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in naked flesh, such as fingers or toes, and others; and the quality of their use is that when you find leeches that are in clean sweet water without any dirt, you take them; and put one in sweet water, until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then let him be bled from a vein and with cupping glasses, then rub the member until it turns red, and place the leeches on; and when they are full, and bite, if it is a place where one can place a cupping glass, put one on, for that is much better.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the vein with a needle, and then with water, very well, and then press it; and if the vein is too tight after the body of the leeches, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on top, until the bleeding stops; and if the bleeding increases, place ground vitriol, or galls, and similar things, on top, until it stops; or you place half a handful of peeled peas on the site, and leave them until they turn green at the site, and it will now stop; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches will not attach, then rub the bleeding site with fresh blood, or poke the vein with a needle until the blood comes out, and then place the leeches on top, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they are defecating, then sprinkle a little powder of ground aloe and salt, or ash, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish people who gaze upon this chapter will not find it in any of the ancient books or letters; and for this reason, knowledge is strange in our land, for I have never found a good one; and I know nothing about it, except through the knowledge of the ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have gained understanding, and through experience and the custom of my life. And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained within, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us say in the prologue of this book the sums of the words and the chapters where the sage sets his understanding, and remains on truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crush injury befalls someone, you must hurry to treat the patient from both sides with a hot poultice, if nothing else binds him, such as weakness of body, or fever, or old age; and if the weather is not very warm, or too cold; and eat cold foods, that is, cold eggs, and milk and cheese from a goat or kid, and drink no wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill himself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you suspect a hot abscess, or spreading of matter in the limb; then return the patient to his former treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, one should feed the patient foods that promote swelling and粘性, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testes, feet, pig stomach, offal, fresh fish, and thick wine, and similar things.Et li carnes qui sont de colde norrissement, si conviennent qu’on le fasse manger a grant fin, ou il ait grand besoin; car l’os qui est brisié ne voudroit mie demourer en lieu chaut et colde, s’il le pot eviter.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And meats that are of cold nature should be eaten in moderation, or when there is great need; because a broken bone does not want to stay in a hot and cold place if it can be avoided. For with cool swelling, bruises heal faster.And the meats which are of hot norrissement, si conviennent qu’on le fasse manger en petit quanitite et en grant fin ou il ne se veult mie demourer; car l’os qui est brisié ne voudroit mie demourer en lieu colde et chaut s’il le pot eviter.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well set or joined according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children; but have no concern, reset the broken bone using the large tendons that stretch and join the limb together, so that it is forced into its former position; do not stop at all in his work, and for this reason one should nourish themselves with plenty of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that there are various types of fractures in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter about all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is one fracture that goes to the bone, and another in sharpening, as with the point of a writing quill.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, then it is all one small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each part has its own technique and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory comes to mind; and the break in the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted, and it appears clearly when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twistiness nor pain in the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but it can have a twist, or a split, or a minor fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with your hand, but apply remedies that are mentioned below, and then hold it firmly and gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes into the bone, and are the two parts separated, they should now be put in place equally, so that hot abscesses may come; and if cold abscesses come, then let it rest for a day, until the abscess is soothed; then put it equal to the movement that you can easily and gently, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restoration of that which has pieces; then constrain it, as it should be done thereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, whether it is two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or your hand, if it is a small limb, or two tendons, or one tendon and your hand; and put the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, then put them back into place by all means, according to the movement that you can, and be careful that your work does not cause the patient injury or pain; and join well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it does not seem right; then set it well, and do not twist or press too hard as those who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb by their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.
