Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap around the fracture a thick bandage doubled into two or three layers, and leave the excess, then flex the leg so that the heels come to the root of the foot, and weave a long thread between the thigh and the leg next to the knee underneath, and bring the ends of the thread up from above; then wrap around the leg and thigh with the bandage, then put splints on the fracture, and put one splint on top of the bone in the leg; then press the space between the leg and the thigh with soft pieces of cloth to make it even, then start binding firmly three turns or four over the fracture; and as you go higher above the fracture, bind less tightly; then tie the two ends of the thread that you wove between the leg and the thigh, and put three splints on top, then return under the foot to the bottom of the thread, and tighten it so that it doesn’t move out of place, then leave it like this, so that no abscess or swelling or anything else comes of it.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if something happens there, then loosen it and address what is happening, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that are sticking out, they should be removed if possible; and if not, the area should be split open and cleaned out; and the wound is treated as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken in this way with splints, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, this treatment does not help the patient at all.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in one day, or a little less or more, according to the different complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the joint of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is little breaking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a split, or a perforation, and it happens to everyone, with or without pain, and everyone feels it.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one puts something equal to what is broken in its place, as long as it can be put together; then put on the plaster, and if necessary, put a round splint, and bind it as it should be, then follow all the instructions we have given for other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar things; then treat each accident as it needs, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is properly called the "mustelz", and the other is called the "foscile". All injuries occur as they do in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as for the arm, and the procedures are all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns completely inside out.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if only the small bones are broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and it is visible, and it turns inward.Et s’il est brisiez par la garniture de li gros os, si avient que on le voi, et sent dolor, et ne tornet pas; et est grant maladiz.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then achieve extension, and make it even, and tie the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly, and there are several pieces, then the extension should be less and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, then take two wooden splints that reach from the knee to just below the break on either side of the leg; then wrap two bands around them above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this point the leg should not be able to decline to the right or left, and so is well; and some administer a block under the leg that reaches from the foot up to the knee, and they place the leg upon it to prevent movement, and properly they do this in the break where there is injury; and move the leg every day to see if there is any hot abscess or other accident; and treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the break of the bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break, but at times there is a break in the bones of the foot and the two bones of the little toe, and there are various dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones of the leg are broken, and you see the bones on top of each other, then put the patient's foot down on the ground as if he were going to walk, and then put your own foot on top of his where the bones are raised, then press them until they return to their proper place; then apply the ointment and bandages, and place a small wooden board under the leg's belly, then wrap it with cloth and other things as needed.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, for you will find that the bones are healed, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the toes are broken, treat them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint on the broken toe, according to its length, and let it be a little wider; then place under the foot that small wooden board I mentioned before, and tighten it in place. And if there are two or three, or more, broken toes, place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and tighten the board underneath the foot; and let the top of the board press firmly against the belly of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you should not forget the other things that I have said about the other fractures, since we have spoken of them; and treat each case as it deserves.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the shoulder
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, make her sit upright and lean forward slightly from the waist, then fill the natural wound with cotton wool, and put in as many pieces as there are; then make the woman stand up, and gently lift her back little by little, so that the cotton comes out until it reaches the entrance to the nature, and the bone will return with the cotton; and when she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated put it back in, and do this for seven days. Then the fracture will be restored, and if you wish take a lamb's bladder, attach a tube to the opening, fill the bladder with air by blowing into the tube until it is swollen inside; the nature will then return the bone; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the man's elbow is broken, or that of the woman, restore it as we have said for the bone of the hip; and these breaks are not hidden from him who devotes himself to its study and practice, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break reveals in many ways the right path to restoration; understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and insert it into the penis; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or more, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	from breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as in the thighbone or shoulderbone or similar, to be treated immediately, as the remedies we have described bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then continue to treat the fracture in that same hour or that day, if no hot abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if painful abscesses arise, let healing await the ninth day, until the abscesses are soothed, and do not touch them on the third or fourth day, for you would bring about an evil outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible underneath the uncovered chest, you should gently put it back into place with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if extension does not work to put it back into place by hand, then reset it using this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and the width depends on the size of the wound; and for this, the surgeon needs to hold it with a grip of three or four fingers, depending on what he requires in each case of broken bone; and it should be round and slightly thick so that it does not bend under pressure when you work on the limb, and tapered at the front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called 'elbow', because the curved head of the bone should be placed upon the visible end of the bone; and the joint is pressed together once, so that it returns and becomes even with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, then you must chip away at the head of the bone so that the instrument can gain purchase.Et se li os de l’ajutoire de la hainche sont brisiez, si le contremande et le ramaine ensi com il a este brisie; et li estrumens contremande l’os en une furee et li ramaine sus l’autre, tant k’il soit igal.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, either a chisel or a saw, to your ability; then scrape away what is stuck in the bone of harshness and fine shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, you may know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So do what you can to put it back in its place, then moisten the cloth with red wine, and apply it neatly if there is swelling; and do not put any ointment or other medicine on the wound so that pus and corruption may come to it; then minister an emetic after you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and bandage all around according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constricted by the bandage. And many times fools have done this and caused death or腐烂 on the patient; and let the constriction be gentler than other bruises.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may come to it, as we have said, and you feel pain in the area, then do not put emetics on it; but wrap around, instead of emetics, hard rags, and tie them.Et si li chiés ou l’espaule est desaloiee, et il ne se puet demourer ains qu’il se desaloit adés et qu’il soit remies; et tu veis bien que la dislocation avient alors qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil:
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that there is pus forming on the wound, then remove what you have put on over it completely, and apply an ointment that heals wounds, such as tetrafarmacon and similar remedies.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must loosen the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is healed and closed up.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And one must prepare the limbs in such a way that the bowstring moves easily downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they persist for many days, and it cannot be souded but keeps slipping back, know that there are tiny pieces of bone causing this, so you must probe the wound with a needle, and remove all the loose pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula develops, or any other form of corruption, then it should be treated according to what he says in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when a bone is broken and open on the limb, as in the thigh or shoulder and similar large limbs, do not treat it at all, for often death ensues; but leave it be, and perhaps it will close up after 20 or 30 days, then you may treat the wound if you can, if not, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come over the soudure
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Many times after the healing of a fracture, especially when it is near a joint, there remains an unsightly appearance to the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the pus is fresh: apply astringent medicines like aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, either one or all together, and mix them with styptic wine or with egg white or garlic; and place them on the wound in poultices, and hold it firmly, and do not remove for several days; then loosen it, and start another, until the inflammation is reduced; or apply a well-prepared plaster of pitch, for the nature of pitch is to remove all swelling from the limbs; if the inflammation has turned into hardness like stone, and needs to be removed, scrape off the top, and reveal the excess; or have it cut by a surgeon, so that it is removed, and healed until it is cured.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weakened after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, and the limb remains weak and slender, there are many causes: one is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many ligatures, and the limb could not receive nourishment; or due to excessive bleeding; or from too much movement, and not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, and so it is weakened.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and keep the body relaxed so that blood multiplies in him; and administer bath to him, and give him joy and rest; then put pitch on the limb so that the pitch attracts to it greatly, and often wash with tepid water until the attraction goes into the limb; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	[until the limb is] straight after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; so do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb completely anew, and many fools have done this in our land; and these actions are blamed, and great harm and even death may come from them; nevertheless, if the dislocations and tortures are fresh, they should be washed with warm water, or soft herbs such as leaves of marshmallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar medicines that soften, and you make a softening plaster, such as well-prepared diaquilon, and you take the mucilage of marshmallow, and cook it with tallow of calf's skin or oil of sisament, and make a plaster to spread over it; or you take fat figs, and grind them with horse manure, and similar medicines that soften.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the dislocation is reduced by continually rubbing with moist hands for a long time.Et se li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire est brisiez, si ne le traire mie, car il porra venir en son leu; et s’il ne porresse pas adés, si avient qu’il chere par lui aprés long temp, si cure la plaie.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let motion be applied to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is awakened and hardened like stone, and needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut to the bone with a subtle incision; and put cotton and study into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	And if dislocation comes to anyone, then one must immediately reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the place swells and if it is reset in its place, one must not move it at the hour that it is swollen; many times this brings on spasms and other pains; however, when this happens, let the patient be bled, then let him rest until the abscesses are calm; then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as the cure comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocation from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Then the jaws are dislocated on both sides, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are a little pulled out of their places, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang down towards the feet, and saliva flows from the mouth so that he cannot hold it in, nor close his mouth, and his tongue is wrapped around his speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is entire and complete, then you must reset it quickly and not tarry; and in such a way that the minister grabs the head of the patient, and puts his thumb of one hand into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and let the other fingers be relaxed to make it equal; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And watch her until she returns to her place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the dislocation is difficult, especially when both mandibles are together, then use hot water and oil, until you reset it gently; do not try to force it back into place, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back into alignment and the mouth of the dislocation is closed well without softening, then place dampened cloths on it made from rose oil and wax, then bind it gently with soft bandages; and the patient should sleep on his back, and his head should be resting between two pillows so that he does not move to the right or left, nor should he exert himself in any way, but take light food until the pain is gone and the jaw is healed; then he can eat what he wants lightly, and not exert himself to open his mouth to eat and drink until the jaw is fully healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset within an hour and are not converted to their places, then fevers and usual sores come, and by chance, intestinal problems, and by chance, vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a death sentence. And many die from it within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The armpit cannot be dislocated within its continuance, neither on the inside nor outside; and it has been dislocated sometimes by force, and it is well felt when this happens.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and stretches out his arms; then press the dislocated area firmly with your palm, and it will return to its place; then apply the plaster and bind it, and the shoulder joint which is near the neck cannot dislocate; if it does, and if it dislocates at any time, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the plaster and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way, the shoulder is reset when it has dislocated from its socket.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one way is that it dislocates at the bottom part near the armpit; the second is at the foot of the shoulder; and sometimes it dislocates at the top, but this rarely happens; it does not dislocate at the back or inside for the nerves; often it dislocates underneath towards the armpit, especially in those who are thin, for them it pops out violently; but for those who are stout, it pops out and goes back in slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that there is a concussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells from a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must therefore test it until you are certain, and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And you will recognize a dislocation when it is lower down towards the armpit, and there will be a noticeable difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one; and you will find a pit at the top of the shoulder, and under the armpit at the bottom of the shoulder, it will feel like a hollow, just as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way; and also, if it is dislocated at the top, it will not be hidden, for you will see it clearly at the bottom; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to fix when it is new, or when the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the assistant to lift the sick hand up, then place your knees under the shoulder, and pull the joint forcefully upwards in its place; and the assistant lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it back down; this should be done quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If it does not return within a few days as we have said, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and they should be given a mild, soothing poultice, such as a decoction of alfalfa, fenugreek, and sweet clover in water, and they should be laid out on their back, and a pillow of wool equal in thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the shoulder, then the patient's heel should be placed on the pillow, and the top of the shoulder gently pulled up, and one minister should hold the head of the patient so that it does not move down; in this way, the shoulder will return immediately, and you should see to it that it is reset according to this method. You should also have a man present who is taller than the patient; he should stand opposite the patient's side, press his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift up the arm so that the patient hangs from it; then another minister should pull the patient's hand down toward their stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the patient is too weak, they can be helped with something heavy, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is reset in another way: a long stick is placed in the ground, so that the shoulder is as wide as the palm of the hand, and is neither too thick nor too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but with a linen cloth on top, and the patient should be standing upright; then his hand is extended downward on the other side, and the joint will return to its place immediately; and if it does not return for all these things that we have said, then this treatment is performed: take a stick two arms long and four digits wide, which has a pointed tip to easily enter under the shoulder, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie it onto the top of the shoulder with soft cloth so that the shoulder does not burn the patient; then place it under the joint of the patient. Extend his arm along the length of the staff, and tie the shoulder to the staff, and the arm to the tip of the hand; then place the arm on a shield four fingers wide, and extend the hand downward, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever way it is, you must put under the joint a sphere of wool equal in size, then apply the plaster prepared with flour from the mill, frankincense, and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around it; then tighten it under the joint gradually, and tie the string over the plaster, and embrace the hand to his chest, and let his hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And one must eat little while the limbs are being comforted, for he will heal more quickly; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move him; and if he is stiff and not softened, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of place because of moisture that it has acquired, or for another reason, then you must administer cauterizations to three openings, as it is described in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm upward, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are torn or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never return to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations that are towards the bottom, at the breasts, or behind, are made by pushing and stretching with the hands, and one administers them in another way; and treat it until it is healed.Li dislocation qui sont devers lou haut et les costes, si font par estendement, et li cauteres on li met a l’entour des costes sus la piere, car li nerfs sont tenduz sus la piere sus les costes, et li membres sont tenduz ou est la dislocation.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there is aching in the limb, and with movement it becomes worse, then the patient should be bled many times until that ache is alleviated and returns to its former state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of dislocation of the neck
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You should know that the joint of the neck is dislocated with the fingers, and it goes back with the fingers; and when it is dislocated from all sides, especially from the front and behind, and the dislocation is not reduced, for one sees and feels it well, and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick armpit with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is crooked, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you should reset it as soon as any abscesses appear, for if the abscesses appear, it will be painful to reset; and by chance it may not be able to be fully reset all over, especially when it is at the back; so it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and death may result.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that when it can be reset you should extend its hand with your two hands; and its arms should be spread out, and its hands should press according to the elbow all around, forward and backward, and push at the joint of its fingers together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he bends his hand toward his hand, and pushes from the root of the palm to the elbow which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and that the two ministers extend the arm, and tilt it from each other, so that he does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from each side, then you have wrapped a long double cloth around it; and when the patient has joined the joint with his hand, then anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then press the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is in place, then put on dry ointment with egg white, and press it firmly, and bind the arm to the collar of the sick person, and leave it for a few days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not fitting well, then restart the plaster and the bandage, and leave it for some days until it is firmly in place, then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels great pain after the joint is moved back into place and it has been left alone for a day and a night, then bathe and rub it gently, and press until the pain subsides; or you can put a poultice of fatty mutton suet on the joint, leave it for another day and night, remove it, and then let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, replace the poultice, and then enter the bath again; do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see fit, apply a warm poultice of moist cow manure mixed with butter, leave it on, and it will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is healed, and the return is lighter than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be put back into place gently, at the same time that it was dislocated, as long as the joint is swollen or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And for the movement, put the patient's hand on a table, extend his fingers, and look at how he places his palm, so that it covers the appearance of the joint; then press it until it returns to its normal state; but you must make sure that it is in its proper place. Then have him place the back of his hand on a table for both extension and movement.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, then have the patient lie his hand flat on the table, and the surgeon place his hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it now goes back into place, that is good. If not, then constrain it with a warm poultice over the abscess, and leave it thus without re-adjusting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several attempts, then leave the joint crooked; and do him no harm as long as his hand is swollen, and do not try to straighten anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; there is no other cure but to straighten it with a cautery next to the joint, and by chance nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, then put on the plaster that we have described, then squeeze it and leave it for five days, then loosen it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some swelling, then moisten it with warm water and rub it until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on one side or the other, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the palm; then straighten the finger and push the joint towards the dislocation, as far as it will go; then hold the top of the finger and bend it towards the part that is dislocated; and keep it like this for two days, and then straighten it that same day; and don’t bind it as we have said before, and loosen it every day, and make it move, and then rebind it at night; and do this often until it is healed; and do the same if it is dislocated on the palm, and do as you did before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the dislocation of the shoulder blade from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade from the back or neck is dislocated, there is no cure, for death comes quickly with this injury.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the evacuations are without voluntary effort, and he cannot hold them in, and often a limb becomes paralyzed, either both legs or both arms or one leg; and often the sciatic nerve is paralyzed in four places; when it is paralyzed in the back, it is called "gilbositez"; the cure is to find out whether the gilbositez came on in childhood: if so, there is no cure or recovery from it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient ways of curing it with great words are described; but they have not great benefit in all cases; but I have abbreviated them according to my understanding, and have devised instruments in diverse ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the paralysis which comes to the front foot, there is no cure or recovery; and also that which comes directly to both sides, and cannot be cured except by that which comes properly to the back, as I said; and it is so that the patient extends his face in one place evenly, and has a bandage under him, so that he does not bend; then insert a brand at the head into the ground firmly, and another at the feet; and two servants hold the bandages, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the brands; and they are tied well, the brand as we have said, and the nurse puts her palms on the spine firmly, until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this cure, take a board three yards long, and dig under the wall, and let the patient lie on his side, and insert the end of the board under the wall; then place the middle of the board on the spine, and put the patient's feet on the other end of the board, and press hard until it returns to its place. And if you see fit, do this around the turn that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you shall fix two torches at the head of the patient, one yard long, and towards the feet, two others; and there should be between each torch, above and below, a palm's width of space; and in each torch there should be an opening, where the rope runs through, and the torches are firmly planted in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of torches, there should be a twisting torch, over which the ropes twist, and there should be two small torches, a palm's length, on the twisting torches for turning the ropes; then tie the rope that is among the pulleys to the pulley towards the head, and the other rope to the other pulley towards the feet, and each of the ministers turns their pulley to all the rope, and the master puts the spine level as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, then put on a desiccant plaster with plenty of egg, and then the towels, and then the cast of a tablet three inches long, which purples the area of the hernia and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a ligature, as we have said, and use the patient's subtle cooling medicine until he is healed; and if anything comes in the end of health, then one must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the cast that we mentioned earlier; and sometimes they administer a piece of plaster, and sometimes the appearance comes in the lower spine in the back, and they think it is a dislocation; and it is the bone that protrudes, so one should not have any presumption about it: it might bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the shoulder only result in dislocations, and not as with other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: within and without, and before and behind; and more within, and slightly dislocated before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, the sick one is longer, and the sick knee joint protrudes more than the healthy one, and the sick one cannot bend his knee to the fire; and the part which is nearby is swollen with a hot abscess because the head of the thigh bone has come there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of those who have a discharge are contrary to those mentioned earlier.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of those who have it in front are that their leg is well according to its length; nevertheless, they cannot bend their knee without pain, and if they want to walk, they cannot, and they retain their urine, and the groin swells, and when they go, they pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of those who have it behind are that they cannot bend or straighten their knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin is soft, and the head of the thigh is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this type of dislocation are as follows: examine whether the dislocation is recent or old, and if it persists according to its nature, there should be no concern; and no presumptuousness should be shown.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one in which the dislocation is fresh and there are four types of dislocations, quickly return the joint to its place, stretching it inward and outward, moving it to the right and left; perhaps it will return to its place and require no further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, then you must prepare a strong minister, and stretch the leg hard with two hands, or with one arm bound above the knee; and another minister stretches his hand over it in such a way that he presses his hands under his heels, then binds him with a rope around the thigh; and another holds his head with a rope; and they all stretch upward and downward at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then one must apply a splint to the affected part. When the dislocation is in the hip, you should support the patient on his healthy side, then place the rope around the root of the thigh, and the part underneath the armpit; then tighten the rope upward toward the armpit and the groin; then have another minister seize his arms and embrace the thick part of the dislocated thigh, and stretch it forcefully: thus it will return to its place at once. This method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot pull it in the manner we have said, then you should tie the patient's two feet together with a strong rope under the two heels, and over the two knees, and let the affected leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then let him be hung by the head of a pole, and let his arms hang two lengths from the ground; then command a minister to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another minister hang with the patient, embracing the thigh firmly, for the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is out of place, let the patient lie as we have said in the one who has lameness, and tighten the rope on the affected leg properly, and on the thigh also; then put two brands, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert the brand between the thighs of the patient in the middle; and have layers of moist cloth laid around it so that it does not burn the patient, then extend each minister toward him, and let the minister apply pressure equal to his hand on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it goes back, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on a table and press him as we have said in the treatment for dislocation, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, one should extend the affected leg gently, and according to what I have said; and the assistant should put his weight on the painful shoulder, then press with the other hand, and push it downward towards the knee.Et s’il ne veut aler, si covient le lever sus li pels de la gamba malaide, et li mires mette sa main en l’angre malaide, et presse ensi com nos avons dit; car il doit aler ou il nule point aler.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the hip, then one should not stretch the patient downward or raise him up from the ground, but he should remain as though his hip were dislocated on the side, as we have said about lying on both hips; and let him be on his face with the bandage stretched as we have said before, and someone should press upon the joint on the table; and when the patient stretches out his legs and they are even, then one must bring the thighs closer together and apply the ointment and constrain it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three or four days, then loosen it and apply the ointment again; and if you see that they are even, then constrain it as before and leave it for three days; then loosen it and let him walk well as long as the limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	There are three ways that the knee can be dislocated: that is, inside, outside, and behind; it cannot be dislocated in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not stick to his thigh, then you know he is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit up straight, and extend his leg if he can, and lay your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee slowly; and another minister extends his foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he sticks his leg to his thigh lightly; and apply the plaster, and let the leg air-dry at the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three or four days, then loosen it; and do not have the patient walk until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if there is no pain, then administer it strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	Heels are sometimes dislocated, and sometimes fully dislocated, within and without.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it hurts when pressed on the affected part; the movements are weak, and one should gently stretch out the foot with their hands when it is only sprained.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is healed all over, you should make the patient sit upright, and hold his leg tightly by the ankle; then raise the foot towards your right hand, and then towards your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and flex it well upwards; do this twice, as we have said, by bending and stretching the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the operation, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and fix the strap firmly into the ground between his buttocks, and wind cloth around it so that he cannot bend the leg; then hold the leg tightly with one hand at the knee, and another holds the foot stretched out towards their hands or against their thigh; then stretch each hand equally, and the strap should be held firmly between the patient's buttocks to hold them in place as they are stretched; then apply the splint evenly to his hand, and another holds the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at a point, then put the plaster and pads on top, and bind it tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle at the back, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature softens, then tighten it; then loosen it on the third or fourth day, and the patient should start walking in four days; and if he goes before that time, it is not certain that he will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes, you must soothe it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the armpits
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the arms are dislocated, they should be gently extended without force, and that is a minor matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the foot, then you should make the patient sit on a flat surface or table completely upright, and put your foot on top of the affected joint, then press firmly on your foot until it returns to its place; and when it is back in place and there is nothing protruding, then put a two-legged board under the sole of the foot, then tighten it firmly, and leave it for three days, then loosen it; and let him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When injury occurs with dislocation and you wish to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the treatment if you are not wise in the art or have not practiced long, and if you lack compassion and mercy; and do not be rash. Begin with hot poultices to soothe the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand if there is no hope of recovery; but if you see a chance, then immediately bring the limb back into alignment so that the hot poultice can take effect; and once the limb is back in place, administer hot poultices to soothe the wound and treat it with drying ointments as necessary. If there are broken bones or splintered bone fragments due to the dislocation, set the bones and follow our instructions for simple fractures; and beware of rushing into treatment out of fear, as I have said, for this may cause harm according to your Creator's will, and for the safety of your soul and body.
Amen	So be it.
